<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMjQgMjQiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHN0cm9rZT0iY3VycmVudENvbG9yIiBzdHJva2Utd2lkdGg9IjIiIHN0cm9rZS1saW5lY2FwPSJyb3VuZCIgc3Ryb2tlLWxpbmVqb2luPSJyb3VuZCIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgZGF0YS1ybnctaW50LWNsYXNzPSJuZWFyZXN0X19fNzAwXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIiBzdHlsZT0iaGVpZ2h0OjE4cHg7dmVydGljYWwtYWxpZ246bWlkZGxlO3dpZHRoOjE4cHgiPjxwYXRoIGQ9Ik0zIDEyaDE4TTMgNmgxOE0zIDE4aDE4Ij48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-h7gdob" />

src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgNTEyIDUxMiIgZmlsbD0ibm9uZSIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItZXUza2Egci0xYW9ja2lkIiBzdHlsZT0idmVydGljYWwtYWxpZ246bWlkZGxlIj48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTIzMC40MzQgMzc5LjU1NGM4LjI1OSAwIDE0Ljk3OCA2LjcxOSAxNC45NzggMTQuOTc0IDAgOC4yNTYtNi43MTkgMTQuOTc0LTE0Ljk3OCAxNC45NzQtOC4yNTUgMC0xNC45NzQtNi43MTgtMTQuOTc0LTE0Ljk3NCAwLTguMjU1IDYuNzE5LTE0Ljk3NCAxNC45NzQtMTQuOTc0em0yMzUuMTg5LTkyLjc1OGMtOC4yNTkgMC0xNC45NzgtNi43MTktMTQuOTc4LTE0Ljk3NCAwLTguMjU5IDYuNzE5LTE0Ljk3OCAxNC45NzgtMTQuOTc4IDguMjU1IDAgMTQuOTc0IDYuNzE5IDE0Ljk3NCAxNC45NzggMCA4LjI1NS02LjcxOSAxNC45NzQtMTQuOTc0IDE0Ljk3NHptMC02MS4zNTFjLTI1LjU3MSAwLTQ2LjM3NyAyMC44MDUtNDYuMzc3IDQ2LjM3NyAwIDQuOTc5LjgyNyA5LjkzOCAyLjQ2IDE0Ljc1N0wyNjguNTAyIDM2OC4xM2MtOC43MDQtMTIuNTQzLTIyLjgxMi0xOS45NzktMzguMDY4LTE5Ljk3OS0xNy42NzYgMC0zMy43OTEgMTAuMTEzLTQxLjU4NiAyNS45MjRMNTEuMjExIDMwMS41MTRjLTE0LjU0LTcuNjQ2LTI1LjQyNS0zMS41OTUtMjQuMjctNTMuMzkyLjU5OC0xMS4zNzEgNC41My0yMC4xOTYgMTAuNTExLTIzLjYwNCAzLjgtMi4xNTcgOC4zNy0xLjk2OCAxMy4yMTQuNTdsLjkyLjQ4NWMzNi40NjQgMTkuMjEyIDE1NS44MjIgODIuMDc5IDE2MC44NDQgODQuNDEzIDcuNzU3IDMuNTg2IDEyLjA2OSA1LjA0MSAyNS4yNzktMS4yMjJsMjQ2LjcyMy0xMjguMzE3YzMuNjE1LTEuMzY1IDcuODMyLTQuODMgNy44MzItMTAuMDkxIDAtNy4zLTcuNTQ2LTEwLjE3Ny03LjU2OC0xMC4xNzctMTQuMDI2LTYuNzI5LTM1LjYwMS0xNi44MjctNTYuNjM5LTI2LjY3Ni00NC45NjUtMjEuMDU1LTk1LjkzMy00NC45MTktMTE4LjMxOC01Ni42MzktMTkuMzIzLTEwLjExNi0zNC44NzctMS41OS0zNy42NS4xMzVsLTUuMzkgMi42NjdDMTY1Ljk2NSAxMjkuNDgyIDMxLjE1NCAxOTYuMjQ4IDIzLjQ3OSAyMDAuOTE3IDkuNzM1IDIwOS4yOCAxLjIyNCAyMjUuOTQuMTIyIDI0Ni42MjVjLTEuNzIyIDMyLjc4OSAxNS4wMDcgNjYuOTY5IDM4LjkxNiA3OS41MTJsMTQ1LjUzNiA3NS4wNTdjMy4yNzkgMjIuNzA5IDIyLjgyNyAzOS43MTIgNDUuODYgMzkuNzEyIDI1LjMzNyAwIDQ1Ljk5Mi0yMC40MjUgNDYuMzc0LTQ1LjY3MmwxNjAuMjkyLTg2Ljg3YTQ2LjQxIDQ2LjQxIDAgMDAyOC41MjMgOS44MzVjMjUuNTcxIDAgNDYuMzc3LTIwLjgwNiA0Ni4zNzctNDYuMzc3IDAtMjUuNTcyLTIwLjgwNi00Ni4zNzctNDYuMzc3LTQ2LjM3N3oiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjwvc3ZnPg==" # 

<span key="9b277ee498fc4c5dbcf7eec5e30dbad0"><span offset-key="9b277ee498fc4c5dbcf7eec5e30dbad0:0">Test Dirven Development:</span></span>

<img src="https://github.com/bgoonz/gitbook-embeds/blob/master/broken-reference" class="css-9pa8cd" draggable="false" />

# 

<span key="75a22297770946828d245ddb56f00a84"><span offset-key="75a22297770946828d245ddb56f00a84:0">Overview</span></span>

<span key="15217d4372224c7aa26729238c24d520"><span offset-key="15217d4372224c7aa26729238c24d520:0">In computing, error detection is a technique that enables a reliable flow during the execution of the program.</span></span>

<span key="49929438fb1343e59dda3d08d56605bb"><span offset-key="49929438fb1343e59dda3d08d56605bb:0">One approach to error detection is error checking. This method maintains normal program flow with subsequent explicit checks for anomalies, which are reported using specific return values, an auxiliary global variable, or floating-point status flags.</span></span>

<span key="c4fdaa83879d4c399f44aaaf97732804"><span offset-key="c4fdaa83879d4c399f44aaaf97732804:0">An exception is the occurrence of an anomaly during the program execution, which interrupts its normal flow. Such an interruption triggers the execution of a pre-registered exception handler.</span></span>

<span key="d21b50f291534f238884d09e34e20ef4"><span offset-key="d21b50f291534f238884d09e34e20ef4:0">Exceptions can happen both on the software and the hardware level.</span></span>

<span key="773a62665de24d778b834cfe5e77399a"><span offset-key="773a62665de24d778b834cfe5e77399a:0">Exceptions in JavaScript</span></span>

<span key="81cbef059eb1411ab70d9d521a472c9f"><span offset-key="81cbef059eb1411ab70d9d521a472c9f:0">===============-------------------------------------------------------------------=</span></span>

<span key="6b4e009170bd454395272c41153ac8a5"><span offset-key="6b4e009170bd454395272c41153ac8a5:0">A single JavaScript application may have to run on many different operating systems, browsers + plugins, and devices. No matter how many tests you wrote, supporting such an environment of possibilities will ultimately lead to errors.</span></span>

<span key="d9e4ad925e0e4bda8bd84dd216d002d8"><span offset-key="d9e4ad925e0e4bda8bd84dd216d002d8:0">From an end-user's standpoint, JavaScript is dealing with errors by just failing silently. Things are a bit more complicated under the hood.</span></span>

<span key="fb884234a9544cfc80bf6aebb33e64fb"><span offset-key="fb884234a9544cfc80bf6aebb33e64fb:0">A JavaScript code throws an exception when a particular statement generates an error. Instead of executing the next code statement, the </span></span><a href="https://blog.sessionstack.com/how-javascript-works-inside-the-v8-engine-5-tips-on-how-to-write-optimized-code-ac089e62b12e" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="0ed4466447a34feb9708ceebc9905b24" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="b8dd92675be7479b8c819ba104f57efc"><span data-offset-key="b8dd92675be7479b8c819ba104f57efc:0">JavaScript engine</span></span></span></a><span key="30da23ab0ae94645a6be0fee74097973"><span offset-key="30da23ab0ae94645a6be0fee74097973:0"> checks for the existence of exception handling code.</span></span>

<span key="957549f3226848c9aee5c6743494b502"><span offset-key="957549f3226848c9aee5c6743494b502:0">If no exception handlers have been defined, the engine returns from the function that threw the exception. This process is repeated for each function on the </span></span><a href="https://blog.sessionstack.com/how-does-javascript-actually-work-part-1-b0bacc073cf" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="48ac64bfda9b4d51af94eca0adf8dac0" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="ed21bd3657724a2fa3043eaf2cd61ed4"><span data-offset-key="ed21bd3657724a2fa3043eaf2cd61ed4:0">call stack</span></span></span></a><span key="ad4036c32f844ce29b69375d01b1e46c"><span offset-key="ad4036c32f844ce29b69375d01b1e46c:0"> until it finds an exception handler. If no exception handler is found and there are no more functions on the stack, the next function on the callback queue is added to the stack by the event loop.</span></span>

<span key="604970fc8c454483b91dcb6bbe89d7bf"><span offset-key="604970fc8c454483b91dcb6bbe89d7bf:0">When an exception occurs, an Error Object is created and thrown.</span></span>

<span key="96b67eb6cda0470c8c12929811a79ca7"><span offset-key="96b67eb6cda0470c8c12929811a79ca7:0">Types of Error Objects</span></span>

<span key="732ac4e2df774d4cab56976a94aa7459"><span offset-key="732ac4e2df774d4cab56976a94aa7459:0">=================-------------------------------------------------------------------=</span></span>

<span key="e389239c3aaf43b8bab4a10912d2995b"><span offset-key="e389239c3aaf43b8bab4a10912d2995b:0">There are nine types of built-in error objects in JavaScript, which are the foundation for exception handling:</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="8adf2e2568054567a6daf9ef80bafe14"><span offset-key="8adf2e2568054567a6daf9ef80bafe14:0">Error --- represents generic exceptions. It is most often used for implementing user-defined exceptions.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="8dabfb87ff344002b691cac36997b452"><span offset-key="8dabfb87ff344002b691cac36997b452:0">EvalError --- occurs when the </span>`eval()`<span offset-key="8dabfb87ff344002b691cac36997b452:2"> function is used improperly.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="c5376fe8b76b444c93367f0c223aa314"><span offset-key="c5376fe8b76b444c93367f0c223aa314:0">RangeError --- used for errors that occur when a numeric variable or parameter is outside of its valid range.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="2a29bec93b8a432ca05bc4e23813b555"><span offset-key="2a29bec93b8a432ca05bc4e23813b555:0">ReferenceError --- occurs when a non-existent variable is accessed.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="1aa83c829efb45e5b969b1014235b73e"><span offset-key="1aa83c829efb45e5b969b1014235b73e:0">SyntaxError --- occurs when the JavaScript language rules are broken. For static-typed languages, this happens during compilation time. In JavaScript, it happens during runtime.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="ada5c2631edd43968e1ecefdad043e1b"><span offset-key="ada5c2631edd43968e1ecefdad043e1b:0">TypeError --- occurs when a value does not match the expected type. Calling a non-existent object method is a common cause of this type of exception.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="6ce5e74342c34855857c6277d52fca16"><span offset-key="6ce5e74342c34855857c6277d52fca16:0">URIError --- occurs when </span>`encodeURI()`<span offset-key="6ce5e74342c34855857c6277d52fca16:2"> and </span>`decodeURI()`<span offset-key="6ce5e74342c34855857c6277d52fca16:4"> encounter a malformed URI.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="d7e8381aaae64cdd89037316624fccda"><span offset-key="d7e8381aaae64cdd89037316624fccda:0">AggregateError --- when multiple errors need to be reported by an operation, for example by </span>`Promise.any()`<span offset-key="d7e8381aaae64cdd89037316624fccda:2">.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="b2b633e9292743669f4aa2c2254b204d"><span offset-key="b2b633e9292743669f4aa2c2254b204d:0">InternalError --- occurs when an internal error in the JavaScript engine is thrown. E.g. "too much recursion". This API is not standardized at the moment of writing this article.</span></span>

<span key="e23c2b67ca7c45d89bd63901c6e675f9"><span offset-key="e23c2b67ca7c45d89bd63901c6e675f9:0">You can also define custom error types by inheriting some of the built-in error types.</span></span>

<span key="08b2b22427bb4a0c93ae6b595e3d3779"><span offset-key="08b2b22427bb4a0c93ae6b595e3d3779:0">Throwing Exceptions</span></span>

<span key="b3c7a7f759ff419e94ef7aade91cb27c"><span offset-key="b3c7a7f759ff419e94ef7aade91cb27c:0">===================-------------------------------------------------------------------</span></span>

<span key="92a5029871614beaac150b7c6e590a23"><span offset-key="92a5029871614beaac150b7c6e590a23:0">JavaScript allows developers to trigger exceptions via the </span>`throw`<span offset-key="92a5029871614beaac150b7c6e590a23:2"> statement.</span></span>

<span key="f4002aac88b9421aac782ee3ce07ba01"><span offset-key="f4002aac88b9421aac782ee3ce07ba01:0">Each of the built-in error objects takes an optional "message" parameter that gives a human-readable description of the error.</span></span>

<span key="cd58472c5abd468c80afa33aa496c800"><span offset-key="cd58472c5abd468c80afa33aa496c800:0">It's important to note that you can </span>`throw`<span offset-key="cd58472c5abd468c80afa33aa496c800:2"> any type of object as an Exception, such as Numbers, Strings, Arrays, etc.</span></span>

<span key="e54e1ea1da55415d9590eb816328605f"><span offset-key="e54e1ea1da55415d9590eb816328605f:0">These are all valid JavaScript statements.</span></span>

<span key="7b50e718911b47fba255c948a80cd441"><span offset-key="7b50e718911b47fba255c948a80cd441:0">There are benefits to using the built-in error types instead of other objects since some browsers give special treatment to them, such as the name of the file which caused the exception, the line number, and the stack trace. Some browsers, like Firefox, are populating these properties for all types of objects.</span></span>

<span key="49c505a0bf37484a9b7ce5193c849b50"><span offset-key="49c505a0bf37484a9b7ce5193c849b50:0">Handling Exceptions</span></span>

<span key="c6bceb9bb84e4eabb207208d06ae2921"><span offset-key="c6bceb9bb84e4eabb207208d06ae2921:0">===================-------------------------------------------------------------------</span></span>

<span key="bca67f7ed56c45ee8923f0c065023bb3"><span offset-key="bca67f7ed56c45ee8923f0c065023bb3:0">Now we will see how to make sure that exceptions don't crash our apps.</span></span>

## 

<span key="3adb09ce12f24d41a724753381170831"><span offset-key="3adb09ce12f24d41a724753381170831:0">The "try" Clause</span></span>

<span key="b594cf612d374a86bf5e8de1c73ebf15"><span offset-key="b594cf612d374a86bf5e8de1c73ebf15:0">JavaScript, quite similar to other programming languages, has the </span>`try`<span offset-key="b594cf612d374a86bf5e8de1c73ebf15:2">, </span>`catch`<span offset-key="b594cf612d374a86bf5e8de1c73ebf15:4">, </span>`finally`<span offset-key="b594cf612d374a86bf5e8de1c73ebf15:6"> statements, which gives us control over the flow of exceptions on our code.</span></span>

<span key="8170012d8c6e4c098d9b3daf907b5e3f"><span offset-key="8170012d8c6e4c098d9b3daf907b5e3f:0">Here is a sample:</span></span>

<span key="ae5b0b9a837b470c9076d257e2814021"><span offset-key="ae5b0b9a837b470c9076d257e2814021:0">The </span>`try`<span offset-key="ae5b0b9a837b470c9076d257e2814021:2"> clause is mandatory and wraps a block of code that potentially can throw an error.</span></span>

## 

<span key="a5b55cf817d744109abb7bf9fb9d6c8a"><span offset-key="a5b55cf817d744109abb7bf9fb9d6c8a:0">The "catch" Clause</span></span>

<span key="127cbccfce2349a0baf33e9e657bd972"><span offset-key="127cbccfce2349a0baf33e9e657bd972:0">It is followed by a </span>`catch`<span offset-key="127cbccfce2349a0baf33e9e657bd972:2"> block, which wraps JavaScript code that handles the error.</span></span>

<span key="84896e1172434637bee4b4edf42431e3"><span offset-key="84896e1172434637bee4b4edf42431e3:0">The </span>`catch`<span offset-key="84896e1172434637bee4b4edf42431e3:2"> clause stops the exception from propagating through the call stack and allows the application flow to continue. The error itself is passed as an argument to the </span>`catch`<span offset-key="84896e1172434637bee4b4edf42431e3:4"> clause.</span></span>

<span key="46b7a804cf9e47e6b2d0a32d35f9e813"><span offset-key="46b7a804cf9e47e6b2d0a32d35f9e813:0">Commonly, some code blocks can throw a different kind of exception, and your application can potentially act differently depending on the exception.</span></span>

<span key="79c96d18ae964680823dc166e111c5da"><span offset-key="79c96d18ae964680823dc166e111c5da:0">JavaScript exposes the </span>`instanceof`<span offset-key="79c96d18ae964680823dc166e111c5da:2"> operator that can be used to differentiate between the types of exceptions:</span></span>

<span key="d3b02a97778449a0959f36ea2bbcfd7a"><span offset-key="d3b02a97778449a0959f36ea2bbcfd7a:0">It's a valid case to re-</span>`throw`<span offset-key="d3b02a97778449a0959f36ea2bbcfd7a:2"> an exception that has been caught. For example, if you catch an exception, the type of which is not relevant to you in this context.</span></span>

## 

<span key="4c16e6b916184391bc59e32e63be5674"><span offset-key="4c16e6b916184391bc59e32e63be5674:0">The "finally" Clause</span></span>

<span key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7"><span offset-key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7:0">The </span>`finally`<span offset-key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7:2"> code block is executed after the </span>`try`<span offset-key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7:4"> and </span>`catch`<span offset-key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7:6"> clauses, regardless of any exceptions. The </span>`finally`<span offset-key="493c6f3ac3b240cb8f91648a42ddcaf7:8">clause is useful for including clean up code such as closing WebSocket connections or other resources.</span></span>

<span key="eccb9989c10c4c5f97b125827b214047"><span offset-key="eccb9989c10c4c5f97b125827b214047:0">Note that the </span>`finally`<span offset-key="eccb9989c10c4c5f97b125827b214047:2"> block will be executed even if a thrown exception is not caught. In such a scenario, the </span>`finally`<span offset-key="eccb9989c10c4c5f97b125827b214047:4"> block is executed, and then the engine continues to go through the functions in the call stack in order until the exception is handled properly or the application is terminated.</span></span>

<span key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f"><span offset-key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f:0">Also important to note is that the </span>`finally`<span offset-key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f:2"> block will be executed even if the </span>`try`<span offset-key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f:4"> or </span>`catch`<span offset-key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f:6"> blocks execute a </span>`return`<span offset-key="07867bc9113c4cb18f92ce862fc1a10f:8"> statement.</span></span>

<span key="d0ae5cbfc1894e349eaff6409085d9a2"><span offset-key="d0ae5cbfc1894e349eaff6409085d9a2:0">Let's look at the following example:</span></span>

<span key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6"><span offset-key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6:0">By invoking the </span>`foo1()`<span offset-key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6:2"> function, we get </span>`false`<span offset-key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6:4"> as result, even though the </span>`try`<span offset-key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6:6"> block has a </span>`return`<span offset-key="61622ee95aa44438b031a208893e6bd6:8"> statement.</span></span>

<span key="77bbcb8484ec433d84dc37fcb0dedea1"><span offset-key="77bbcb8484ec433d84dc37fcb0dedea1:0">The same applies if we have a </span>`return`<span offset-key="77bbcb8484ec433d84dc37fcb0dedea1:2"> statement in a </span>`catch`<span offset-key="77bbcb8484ec433d84dc37fcb0dedea1:4"> block:</span></span>

<span key="4078201a1bd147f5a116931d3200d3fa"><span offset-key="4078201a1bd147f5a116931d3200d3fa:0">Invoking </span>`foo2()`<span offset-key="4078201a1bd147f5a116931d3200d3fa:2"> also returns </span>`false`<span offset-key="4078201a1bd147f5a116931d3200d3fa:4">.</span></span>

<span key="dafa4a9419b74bc48fbbceba9411459b"><span offset-key="dafa4a9419b74bc48fbbceba9411459b:0">Handling Exceptions in Asynchronous Code</span></span>

<span key="b139363aa77e40ab9582956cbe6c2fc1"><span offset-key="b139363aa77e40ab9582956cbe6c2fc1:0">===================-------------------------------------------------------------------</span></span>

<span key="cf2c47a86832469e8550ffd8a36c7f4e"><span offset-key="cf2c47a86832469e8550ffd8a36c7f4e:0">Custom errors, extending Error When we develop something, we often need our own error classes to reflect specific things that may go wrong in our tasks. For errors in network operations we may need HttpError, for database operations DbError, for searching operations NotFoundError and so on.</span></span>

<span key="12fafb42ab7240e187470b1281289e50"><span offset-key="12fafb42ab7240e187470b1281289e50:0">Our errors should support basic error properties like message, name and, preferably, stack. But they also may have other properties of their own, e.g. HttpError objects may have a statusCode property with a value like 404 or 403 or 500.</span></span>

<span key="9c0916a47ffb434b8768b70bb4f91b2f"><span offset-key="9c0916a47ffb434b8768b70bb4f91b2f:0">JavaScript allows to use throw with any argument, so technically our custom error classes don’t need to inherit from Error. But if we inherit, then it becomes possible to use obj instanceof Error to identify error objects. So it’s better to inherit from it.</span></span>

<span key="77a827547bda4d43807d9f473b339565"><span offset-key="77a827547bda4d43807d9f473b339565:0">As the application grows, our own errors naturally form a hierarchy. For instance, HttpTimeoutError may inherit from HttpError, and so on.</span></span>

<span key="9184b0defe1245b6abc0f8f3578659c0"><span offset-key="9184b0defe1245b6abc0f8f3578659c0:0">Extending Error As an example, let’s consider a function readUser(json) that should read JSON with user data.</span></span>

<span key="b55119b249394f688f482434431965e5"><span offset-key="b55119b249394f688f482434431965e5:0">Here’s an example of how a valid json may look:</span></span>

<span key="4a8cba04a18944d9bb45d27cecf5e27e"><span offset-key="4a8cba04a18944d9bb45d27cecf5e27e:0">let json = </span>`{ "name": "John", "age": 30 }`<span offset-key="4a8cba04a18944d9bb45d27cecf5e27e:2">; Internally, we’ll use JSON.parse. If it receives malformed json, then it throws SyntaxError. But even if json is syntactically correct, that doesn’t mean that it’s a valid user, right? It may miss the necessary data. For instance, it may not have name and age properties that are essential for our users.</span></span>

<span key="848e4d75410e48498042589a75b397d6"><span offset-key="848e4d75410e48498042589a75b397d6:0">Our function readUser(json) will not only read JSON, but check (“validate”) the data. If there are no required fields, or the format is wrong, then that’s an error. And that’s not a SyntaxError, because the data is syntactically correct, but another kind of error. We’ll call it ValidationError and create a class for it. An error of that kind should also carry the information about the offending field.</span></span>

<span key="47b3acb1b0c84b698ade0868a45d434b"><span offset-key="47b3acb1b0c84b698ade0868a45d434b:0">Our ValidationError class should inherit from the Error class.</span></span>

<span key="3925bc428411495dacbb00e2a7e5d1bf"><span offset-key="3925bc428411495dacbb00e2a7e5d1bf:0">The Error class is built-in, but here’s its approximate code so we can understand what we’re extending:</span></span>

<span key="03c1059ec3634d1ea17644646e891e49"><span offset-key="03c1059ec3634d1ea17644646e891e49:0">// The "pseudocode" for the built-in Error class defined by JavaScript itself class Error { constructor(message) { this.message = message; </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="04077b2a8dfd489eace35481298476e1" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="bd80e07129ca4a10ae7520f3abfd2743"><span data-offset-key="bd80e07129ca4a10ae7520f3abfd2743:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="7c36b6a06e8347c1a490bd1ca9fd389d"><span offset-key="7c36b6a06e8347c1a490bd1ca9fd389d:0"> = "Error"; // (different names for different built-in error classes) this.stack = ; // non-standard, but most environments support it } } Now let’s inherit ValidationError from it and try it in action:</span></span>

<span key="c3c7adae601d450489d76cb54d65e8a1"><span offset-key="c3c7adae601d450489d76cb54d65e8a1:0">class ValidationError extends Error { constructor(message) { super(message); // (1) </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="5e297f2747f142c683ce2e24bd9e07b8" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="fbdcaf791a6843749cb343b7738052cc"><span data-offset-key="fbdcaf791a6843749cb343b7738052cc:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="34053591d4594e4193ac82aeb38bd9ae"><span offset-key="34053591d4594e4193ac82aeb38bd9ae:0"> = "ValidationError"; // (2) } }</span></span>

<span key="fd94872e219a4a349f907f5ee5f66683"><span offset-key="fd94872e219a4a349f907f5ee5f66683:0">function test() { throw new ValidationError("Whoops!"); }</span></span>

<span key="36f8e9d6ec95407aa798a09fc748c980"><span offset-key="36f8e9d6ec95407aa798a09fc748c980:0">try { test(); } catch(err) { alert(err.message); // Whoops! alert(</span></span><a href="http://err.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="1c68c15306b447d182a04b80c449f31a" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="a384dd3c2aed49188288b8e787b0319d"><span data-offset-key="a384dd3c2aed49188288b8e787b0319d:0">err.name</span></span></span></a><span key="066c80c86fcf4f4ca2505e630c7709ec"><span offset-key="066c80c86fcf4f4ca2505e630c7709ec:0">); // ValidationError alert(err.stack); // a list of nested calls with line numbers for each } Please note: in the line (1) we call the parent constructor. JavaScript requires us to call super in the child constructor, so that’s obligatory. The parent constructor sets the message property.</span></span>

<span key="ad8a45adec164f6ebdb72e3d70f98dc5"><span offset-key="ad8a45adec164f6ebdb72e3d70f98dc5:0">The parent constructor also sets the name property to "Error", so in the line (2) we reset it to the right value.</span></span>

<span key="7ef5f441ba7f429fad48268f94b52b00"><span offset-key="7ef5f441ba7f429fad48268f94b52b00:0">Let’s try to use it in readUser(json):</span></span>

<span key="7005fdb371ac45d6bc205c13bb3327be"><span offset-key="7005fdb371ac45d6bc205c13bb3327be:0">class ValidationError extends Error { constructor(message) { super(message); </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4c424745a47741ebb63146f210bf1579" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="030c328704184393a9318c2646bc0156"><span data-offset-key="030c328704184393a9318c2646bc0156:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="46966881d8794c9ea44597ad7e892d28"><span offset-key="46966881d8794c9ea44597ad7e892d28:0"> = "ValidationError"; } }</span></span>

<span key="56b0c4bfeae84077a52b43f5aa97c9c9"><span offset-key="56b0c4bfeae84077a52b43f5aa97c9c9:0">// Usage function readUser(json) { let user = JSON.parse(json);</span></span>

<span key="75a0809c56024e4d884b3f807fe5fe50"><span offset-key="75a0809c56024e4d884b3f807fe5fe50:0">if (!user.age) { throw new ValidationError("No field: age"); } if (!</span></span><a href="http://user.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="fbe1d5be332b4d319dfe631522e8b609" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="fb1513c565cb4480a50bf4809ebae8b4"><span data-offset-key="fb1513c565cb4480a50bf4809ebae8b4:0">user.name</span></span></span></a><span key="25687975ac4646afa798ff63457456af"><span offset-key="25687975ac4646afa798ff63457456af:0">) { throw new ValidationError("No field: name"); }</span></span>

<span key="c6ddc7349f77461aa88f7e730b7ff7a7"><span offset-key="c6ddc7349f77461aa88f7e730b7ff7a7:0">return user; }</span></span>

<span key="30ff481742d9487381fec3ee593bc9ab"><span offset-key="30ff481742d9487381fec3ee593bc9ab:0">// Working example with try..catch</span></span>

<span key="c9d4faa5caf64e41a689feff32a52780"><span offset-key="c9d4faa5caf64e41a689feff32a52780:0">try { let user = readUser('{ "age": 25 }'); } catch (err) { if (err instanceof ValidationError) { alert("Invalid data: " + err.message); // Invalid data: No field: name } else if (err instanceof SyntaxError) { // (\*) alert("JSON Syntax Error: " + err.message); } else { throw err; // unknown error, rethrow it (\*\*) } } The try..catch block in the code above handles both our ValidationError and the built-in SyntaxError from JSON.parse.</span></span>

<span key="dccf5238b83e49ca90818d2c4c2021a4"><span offset-key="dccf5238b83e49ca90818d2c4c2021a4:0">Please take a look at how we use instanceof to check for the specific error type in the line (\*).</span></span>

<span key="2b5b90ba2b364ab080378eaa959cb3aa"><span offset-key="2b5b90ba2b364ab080378eaa959cb3aa:0">We could also look at </span></span><a href="http://err.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="7dc90154f10748cf8519ca7ee4738068" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="cb8d9361f6714ca9b156a434a80a991d"><span data-offset-key="cb8d9361f6714ca9b156a434a80a991d:0">err.name</span></span></span></a><span key="f171059ad7be495c9c508a1e453d9ded"><span offset-key="f171059ad7be495c9c508a1e453d9ded:0">, like this:</span></span>

<span key="f566b6872ddd49fbbeb9c05d5c08a0a9"><span offset-key="f566b6872ddd49fbbeb9c05d5c08a0a9:0">// ... // instead of (err instanceof SyntaxError) } else if (</span></span><a href="http://err.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="11d290a7915f4362a161f1ea5cdb0a10" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="50c245f60840450099ae28e9bd9bc9ec"><span data-offset-key="50c245f60840450099ae28e9bd9bc9ec:0">err.name</span></span></span></a><span key="1c04759792e141c9bb2e79bab32bec8f"><span offset-key="1c04759792e141c9bb2e79bab32bec8f:0"> == "SyntaxError") { // (\*) // ... The instanceof version is much better, because in the future we are going to extend ValidationError, make subtypes of it, like PropertyRequiredError. And instanceof check will continue to work for new inheriting classes. So that’s future-proof.</span></span>

<span key="173ad2d8367545aaba36f5b0479a9627"><span offset-key="173ad2d8367545aaba36f5b0479a9627:0">Also it’s important that if catch meets an unknown error, then it rethrows it in the line (\*\*). The catch block only knows how to handle validation and syntax errors, other kinds (caused by a typo in the code or other unknown reasons) should fall through.</span></span>

<span key="9ba6213e093e4085b8048bc714f7ef51"><span offset-key="9ba6213e093e4085b8048bc714f7ef51:0">Further inheritance The ValidationError class is very generic. Many things may go wrong. The property may be absent or it may be in a wrong format (like a string value for age instead of a number). Let’s make a more concrete class PropertyRequiredError, exactly for absent properties. It will carry additional information about the property that’s missing.</span></span>

<span key="54d17959ceec40d0850f090538d4a134"><span offset-key="54d17959ceec40d0850f090538d4a134:0">class ValidationError extends Error { constructor(message) { super(message); </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4dae9615e2e74e158b5b3049764033a5" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="a03a649a534d48e3859f064f6d82adad"><span data-offset-key="a03a649a534d48e3859f064f6d82adad:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="2353591a50144d148bda5fce7ab4bad9"><span offset-key="2353591a50144d148bda5fce7ab4bad9:0"> = "ValidationError"; } }</span></span>

<span key="c9f242fbc4a54312bd4f25506f40860f"><span offset-key="c9f242fbc4a54312bd4f25506f40860f:0">class PropertyRequiredError extends ValidationError { constructor(property) { super("No property: " + property); </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6cf6eda036124ce9a32e18a9605b3a03" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="2a2eb16fc7184726a638e6291e8b9a92"><span data-offset-key="2a2eb16fc7184726a638e6291e8b9a92:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="c9f152ba11b34ddcab513a943b8dca8f"><span offset-key="c9f152ba11b34ddcab513a943b8dca8f:0"> = "PropertyRequiredError"; this.property = property; } }</span></span>

<span key="2302888b376f4d96a11e9a5f2104685b"><span offset-key="2302888b376f4d96a11e9a5f2104685b:0">// Usage function readUser(json) { let user = JSON.parse(json);</span></span>

<span key="6918c6ff0ff14cfd939d053421deb2f8"><span offset-key="6918c6ff0ff14cfd939d053421deb2f8:0">if (!user.age) { throw new PropertyRequiredError("age"); } if (!</span></span><a href="http://user.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="802fc7e8b063405f9c2786956ab36630" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="057c607857504b33a000d802ec960506"><span data-offset-key="057c607857504b33a000d802ec960506:0">user.name</span></span></span></a><span key="d04a3212de824a8cb4cac470ae5a9d9c"><span offset-key="d04a3212de824a8cb4cac470ae5a9d9c:0">) { throw new PropertyRequiredError("name"); }</span></span>

<span key="1106b65462034aa3806c0d9647d66f0c"><span offset-key="1106b65462034aa3806c0d9647d66f0c:0">return user; }</span></span>

<span key="f85d27e09a53465c9efdd2fe9b295a3f"><span offset-key="f85d27e09a53465c9efdd2fe9b295a3f:0">// Working example with try..catch</span></span>

<span key="b83a57dca5dd4681b630383a7a0b2194"><span offset-key="b83a57dca5dd4681b630383a7a0b2194:0">try { let user = readUser('{ "age": 25 }'); } catch (err) { if (err instanceof ValidationError) { alert("Invalid data: " + err.message); // Invalid data: No property: name alert(</span></span><a href="http://err.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9090ff5b193d4cf9a07994394919aa75" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="086975988a044f01ab375101f818ca97"><span data-offset-key="086975988a044f01ab375101f818ca97:0">err.name</span></span></span></a><span key="84ed3953ca92410595cbdcd8ceea9f33"><span offset-key="84ed3953ca92410595cbdcd8ceea9f33:0">); // PropertyRequiredError alert(err.property); // name } else if (err instanceof SyntaxError) { alert("JSON Syntax Error: " + err.message); } else { throw err; // unknown error, rethrow it } } The new class PropertyRequiredError is easy to use: we only need to pass the property name: new PropertyRequiredError(property). The human-readable message is generated by the constructor.</span></span>

<span key="1d7fb2ea673a4ccfa68b5216b237160a"><span offset-key="1d7fb2ea673a4ccfa68b5216b237160a:0">Please note that </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6181c3cfc80745b888a0719bab442ac6" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="f072df8ea9b34516b5cee7478366f154"><span data-offset-key="f072df8ea9b34516b5cee7478366f154:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="28f9a3bba50e46cdbabdd10aeeea2c49"><span offset-key="28f9a3bba50e46cdbabdd10aeeea2c49:0"> in PropertyRequiredError constructor is again assigned manually. That may become a bit tedious – to assign </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="0a1cddcdd0fe42e88352bfc97d6369b7" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="8cad64ae4ea9405faa4363c95ec041f9"><span data-offset-key="8cad64ae4ea9405faa4363c95ec041f9:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="641711ee4b3c447699dc49567614cffd"><span offset-key="641711ee4b3c447699dc49567614cffd:0"> = in every custom error class. We can avoid it by making our own “basic error” class that assigns </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="62614ed042614137b373839c13cd77a7" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="dcb1bf4395c74f97b58cf194d00feb1f"><span data-offset-key="dcb1bf4395c74f97b58cf194d00feb1f:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="87641c05a0cd471a9bbc76f2151c5081"><span offset-key="87641c05a0cd471a9bbc76f2151c5081:0"> = </span></span><a href="http://this.constructor.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="b57f5afa53a44c1880d591f8a2b0c7d2" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="3e4da01cdc19498fbcb03c65f70d45ac"><span data-offset-key="3e4da01cdc19498fbcb03c65f70d45ac:0">this.constructor.name</span></span></span></a><span key="c324ae59a6164c329f1168649b1afea8"><span offset-key="c324ae59a6164c329f1168649b1afea8:0">. And then inherit all our custom errors from it.</span></span>

<span key="4e95977d7f0e4c6d8a8a6578519135db"><span offset-key="4e95977d7f0e4c6d8a8a6578519135db:0">Let’s call it MyError.</span></span>

<span key="8e95437258fa4529992fae60a72e7fdf"><span offset-key="8e95437258fa4529992fae60a72e7fdf:0">Here’s the code with MyError and other custom error classes, simplified:</span></span>

<span key="ab26df3575c24148ab62bdc11091a0f2"><span offset-key="ab26df3575c24148ab62bdc11091a0f2:0">class MyError extends Error { constructor(message) { super(message); </span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="26ba76e158494a59981ea15ae1198a84" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="6a28fbdbccf843a683a0e5f8531902c5"><span data-offset-key="6a28fbdbccf843a683a0e5f8531902c5:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="c7056bc4d7f04678b526aa97c0598226"><span offset-key="c7056bc4d7f04678b526aa97c0598226:0"> = </span></span><a href="http://this.constructor.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9326c84c5c6e4bccaa130d72538bcb1e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="0879a8c9499b4983b859125edbf2a049"><span data-offset-key="0879a8c9499b4983b859125edbf2a049:0">this.constructor.name</span></span></span></a><span key="f106f7eb113444a7bdbcc8949202618d"><span offset-key="f106f7eb113444a7bdbcc8949202618d:0">; } }</span></span>

<span key="f226c054dff0429c9c0e733acbfa51c0"><span offset-key="f226c054dff0429c9c0e733acbfa51c0:0">class ValidationError extends MyError { }</span></span>

<span key="3189bc5999ed4fa3a3c42b65883e7c54"><span offset-key="3189bc5999ed4fa3a3c42b65883e7c54:0">class PropertyRequiredError extends ValidationError { constructor(property) { super("No property: " + property); this.property = property; } }</span></span>

<span key="a494ef8735fe49cd9f126dc423ce5284"><span offset-key="a494ef8735fe49cd9f126dc423ce5284:0">// name is correct alert( new PropertyRequiredError("field").name ); // PropertyRequiredError Now custom errors are much shorter, especially ValidationError, as we got rid of the "</span></span><a href="http://this.name" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="57b3a77972f54379b00d41bdbb4db345" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="a917f6ddc92146fa831918f8dc0f1f65"><span data-offset-key="a917f6ddc92146fa831918f8dc0f1f65:0">this.name</span></span></span></a><span key="41e91e78c446447dba1bdd86c858c438"><span offset-key="41e91e78c446447dba1bdd86c858c438:0"> = ..." line in the constructor.</span></span>

<span key="6482957107024f38aa255c16a483e186"><span offset-key="6482957107024f38aa255c16a483e186:0">Wrapping exceptions The purpose of the function readUser in the code above is “to read the user data”. There may occur different kinds of errors in the process. Right now we have SyntaxError and ValidationError, but in the future readUser function may grow and probably generate other kinds of errors.</span></span>

<span key="4cc801a43447452797f680f64b406b23"><span offset-key="4cc801a43447452797f680f64b406b23:0">The code which calls readUser should handle these errors. Right now it uses multiple ifs in the catch block, that check the class and handle known errors and rethrow the unknown ones.</span></span>

<span key="4567b696aedb4a169c2ffa61d50d459e"><span offset-key="4567b696aedb4a169c2ffa61d50d459e:0">The scheme is like this:</span></span>

<span key="e89e0f7762324266913b6bdfdc1f6687"><span offset-key="e89e0f7762324266913b6bdfdc1f6687:0">try { ... readUser() // the potential error source ... } catch (err) { if (err instanceof ValidationError) { // handle validation errors } else if (err instanceof SyntaxError) { // handle syntax errors } else { throw err; // unknown error, rethrow it } } In the code above we can see two types of errors, but there can be more.</span></span>

<span key="b024d985b5ef41368fa7cd4e21869942"><span offset-key="b024d985b5ef41368fa7cd4e21869942:0">If the readUser function generates several kinds of errors, then we should ask ourselves: do we really want to check for all error types one-by-one every time?</span></span>

<span key="18e7289db5304baa94229c72ce445003"><span offset-key="18e7289db5304baa94229c72ce445003:0">Often the answer is “No”: we’d like to be “one level above all that”. We just want to know if there was a “data reading error” – why exactly it happened is often irrelevant (the error message describes it). Or, even better, we’d like to have a way to get the error details, but only if we need to.</span></span>

<span key="b3ca05a5fdb8490ab621126b1eedf79e"><span offset-key="b3ca05a5fdb8490ab621126b1eedf79e:0">The technique that we describe here is called “wrapping exceptions”.</span></span>

<span key="06e6d79265384fb1ad51fc0a2a10b1c2"><span offset-key="06e6d79265384fb1ad51fc0a2a10b1c2:0">We’ll make a new class ReadError to represent a generic “data reading” error. The function readUser will catch data reading errors that occur inside it, such as ValidationError and SyntaxError, and generate a ReadError instead. The ReadError object will keep the reference to the original error in its cause property. Then the code that calls readUser will only have to check for ReadError, not for every kind of data reading errors. And if it needs more details of an error, it can check its cause property.</span></span>

<span key="bf748725355343bd9af2e35f61ba51c1"><span offset-key="bf748725355343bd9af2e35f61ba51c1:0">Here’s the code that defines ReadError and demonstrates its use in readUser and try..catch:</span></span>

1

<span key="01c6aa9e39004ad0bcecd827accc78c9"><span offset-key="01c6aa9e39004ad0bcecd827accc78c9:0">class ReadError extends Error {</span></span>

2

<span key="bee157f640cf41478a63140f97f575fc"><span offset-key="bee157f640cf41478a63140f97f575fc:0"> constructor(message, cause) {</span></span>

3

<span key="e160bb38e1524742aa50cd2254408b2f"><span offset-key="e160bb38e1524742aa50cd2254408b2f:0">}</span></span>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHByZXNlcnZlYXNwZWN0cmF0aW89InhNaWRZTWlkIG1lZXQiIGRhdGEtcm53LWludC1jbGFzcz0ibmVhcmVzdF9fXzU3OC0yNjgyXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIHItMTBwdHVuNyIgc3R5bGU9InZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxNnB4Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTAgLjVBLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUgMGgxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEuNS41VjRoLTFWMUgxdjloM3YxSC41YS41LjUgMCAwMS0uNS0uNVYuNXoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjxwYXRoIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xpcC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIiBkPSJNNSA1LjVhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUtLjVoMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUuNXYxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEtLjUuNWgtMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLS41LS41di0xMHpNNiA2djloOVY2SDZ6IiBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiPjwvcGF0aD48L3N2Zz4=" class="r-h7gdob r-10ptun7" />

Copied!

<span key="adf68834893c46dc89b127922ecc3561"><span offset-key="adf68834893c46dc89b127922ecc3561:0">In the code above, readUser works exactly as described – catches syntax and validation errors and throws ReadError errors instead (unknown errors are rethrown as usual).</span></span>

<span key="912eb0c7f14a4eaba2bfc65e00bcfba5"><span offset-key="912eb0c7f14a4eaba2bfc65e00bcfba5:0">So the outer code checks instanceof ReadError and that’s it. No need to list all possible error types.</span></span>

<span key="0e5dec0a99164b04888a45a91afa80d3"><span offset-key="0e5dec0a99164b04888a45a91afa80d3:0">The approach is called “wrapping exceptions”, because we take “low level” exceptions and “wrap” them into ReadError that is more abstract. It is widely used in object-oriented programming.</span></span>

<span key="34813ddb50a1415282e23af005f1cefd"><span offset-key="34813ddb50a1415282e23af005f1cefd:0">Summary We can inherit from Error and other built-in error classes normally. We just need to take care of the name property and don’t forget to call super. We can use instanceof to check for particular errors. It also works with inheritance. But sometimes we have an error object coming from a 3rd-party library and there’s no easy way to get its class. Then name property can be used for such checks. Wrapping exceptions is a widespread technique: a function handles low-level exceptions and creates higher-level errors instead of various low-level ones. Low-level exceptions sometimes become properties of that object like err.cause in the examples above, but that’s not strictly required. =================-------------------------------------------------------------------</span></span>

<span key="aaba66691b864e459955c8a3ef5c71b2"><span offset-key="aaba66691b864e459955c8a3ef5c71b2:0">We won't go into detail about the </span></span><a href="https://blog.sessionstack.com/how-javascript-works-event-loop-and-the-rise-of-async-programming-5-ways-to-better-coding-with-2f077c4438b5" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="d186788ebd884bcdb885a4d7a65ee67f" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="abfaf911a1a8440fb2e6b9c6ddc8c560"><span data-offset-key="abfaf911a1a8440fb2e6b9c6ddc8c560:0">internals of async programming in JavaScript</span></span></span></a><span key="00fa818063e745cdbf886b2720890f8f"><span offset-key="00fa818063e745cdbf886b2720890f8f:0"> here, but we will see how handling exceptions is done with "callback functions", "promises", and "async/await".</span></span>

## 

<span key="076cdc12e6f64b828f7869ab54ac5dbc"><span offset-key="076cdc12e6f64b828f7869ab54ac5dbc:0">async/await</span></span>

<span key="445e194bc401429fb9e26540720a8471"><span offset-key="445e194bc401429fb9e26540720a8471:0">Let's define a standard function that just throws an error:</span></span>

<span key="e7a31d558f6d46be890636481b5a72ee"><span offset-key="e7a31d558f6d46be890636481b5a72ee:0">When an error is thrown in an </span>`async`<span offset-key="e7a31d558f6d46be890636481b5a72ee:2"> function, a rejected promise will be returned with the thrown error, equivalent to:</span></span>

<span key="92c491f8bd3f48128ec1ced8caa248e2"><span offset-key="92c491f8bd3f48128ec1ced8caa248e2:0">Let's see what happens when </span>`foo()`<span offset-key="92c491f8bd3f48128ec1ced8caa248e2:2"> is invoked:</span></span>

<span key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68"><span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:0">Since </span>`foo()`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:2"> is </span>`async`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:4">, it dispatches a </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:6">. The code does not wait for the </span>`async`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:8"> function, so there is no actual error to be caught at the moment. The </span>`finally`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:10"> block is executed and then the </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="3890a170d58b40ea8173970d53cd0a68:12"> rejects.</span></span>

<span key="efd4134ccdee4d729d9e1276731c12f9"><span offset-key="efd4134ccdee4d729d9e1276731c12f9:0">We don't have any code that handles this rejected </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="efd4134ccdee4d729d9e1276731c12f9:2">.</span></span>

<span key="e15126b7be3f4e33bb94e9fc4c58dc8d"><span offset-key="e15126b7be3f4e33bb94e9fc4c58dc8d:0">This can be handled by just adding the </span>`await`<span offset-key="e15126b7be3f4e33bb94e9fc4c58dc8d:2"> keyword when invoking </span>`foo()`<span offset-key="e15126b7be3f4e33bb94e9fc4c58dc8d:4"> and wrapping the code in an </span>`async`<span offset-key="e15126b7be3f4e33bb94e9fc4c58dc8d:6"> function:</span></span>

## 

<span key="c63a640d724e4558b4b7d388b3f09fe0"><span offset-key="c63a640d724e4558b4b7d388b3f09fe0:0">Promises</span></span>

<span key="8f16fde3ff81423ab8b7a55a2bb34d57"><span offset-key="8f16fde3ff81423ab8b7a55a2bb34d57:0">Let's define a function that throws an error outside of the </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="8f16fde3ff81423ab8b7a55a2bb34d57:2">:</span></span>

<span key="4b00acaf31ef4255ba9f9555fc5c59b3"><span offset-key="4b00acaf31ef4255ba9f9555fc5c59b3:0">Now let's invoke </span>`foo`<span offset-key="4b00acaf31ef4255ba9f9555fc5c59b3:2"> with a </span>`string`<span offset-key="4b00acaf31ef4255ba9f9555fc5c59b3:4"> instead of a </span>`number`<span offset-key="4b00acaf31ef4255ba9f9555fc5c59b3:6">:</span></span>

<span key="9613aee8805c4d1fb650ffa3f5812d4c"><span offset-key="9613aee8805c4d1fb650ffa3f5812d4c:0">This will result in an </span>`Uncaught TypeError: x is not a number`<span offset-key="9613aee8805c4d1fb650ffa3f5812d4c:2"> since the </span>`catch`<span offset-key="9613aee8805c4d1fb650ffa3f5812d4c:4"> of the promise is not being able to handle an error that was thrown outside of the </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="9613aee8805c4d1fb650ffa3f5812d4c:6">.</span></span>

<span key="5d3d43eae87c40d882dd334843134b7f"><span offset-key="5d3d43eae87c40d882dd334843134b7f:0">To catch such errors, you need to use the standard </span>`try`<span offset-key="5d3d43eae87c40d882dd334843134b7f:2"> and </span>`catch`<span offset-key="5d3d43eae87c40d882dd334843134b7f:4"> clauses:</span></span>

<span key="3d111633fc3d4b7e8e5645a2c08c9683"><span offset-key="3d111633fc3d4b7e8e5645a2c08c9683:0">If </span>`foo`<span offset-key="3d111633fc3d4b7e8e5645a2c08c9683:2"> is modified to throw an error inside of the </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="3d111633fc3d4b7e8e5645a2c08c9683:4">:</span></span>

<span key="3f2931f4adfc42cab6b79428876c03e5"><span offset-key="3f2931f4adfc42cab6b79428876c03e5:0">Now the </span>`catch`<span offset-key="3f2931f4adfc42cab6b79428876c03e5:2"> statement of the promise will handle the error:</span></span>

<span key="066c4e82c65b47c3b05e19f8ffbf5d3d"><span offset-key="066c4e82c65b47c3b05e19f8ffbf5d3d:0">Note that throwing an error inside a </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="066c4e82c65b47c3b05e19f8ffbf5d3d:2"> is the same thing as using the </span>`reject`<span offset-key="066c4e82c65b47c3b05e19f8ffbf5d3d:4"> callback. So it's better to define </span>`foo`<span offset-key="066c4e82c65b47c3b05e19f8ffbf5d3d:6"> like this:</span></span>

<span key="1298636d63874803aeaf0333d6bc59ef"><span offset-key="1298636d63874803aeaf0333d6bc59ef:0">If there is no </span>`catch`<span offset-key="1298636d63874803aeaf0333d6bc59ef:2"> method to handle the error inside the </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="1298636d63874803aeaf0333d6bc59ef:4">, the next function from the callback queue will be added to the stack.</span></span>

## 

<span key="937bae925ed542a6be9f52eb133043a7"><span offset-key="937bae925ed542a6be9f52eb133043a7:0">Callback Functions</span></span>

<span key="621096a1ec6c42f089e638c146764c30"><span offset-key="621096a1ec6c42f089e638c146764c30:0">There are two main rules for working with the error-first callback approach:</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="fd0398e3ef554f5d9038e2b5b36051c1"><span offset-key="fd0398e3ef554f5d9038e2b5b36051c1:0">The first argument of the callback is for the error object. If an error occurred, it will be returned by the first </span>`err`<span offset-key="fd0398e3ef554f5d9038e2b5b36051c1:2"> argument. If no error occurred, </span>`err`<span offset-key="fd0398e3ef554f5d9038e2b5b36051c1:4"> will be set to </span>`null`<span offset-key="fd0398e3ef554f5d9038e2b5b36051c1:6">.</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="c20b8f3fae154aa786b8ad9345906336"><span offset-key="c20b8f3fae154aa786b8ad9345906336:0">The second argument of the callback is the response data.</span></span>

<span key="9039bb1c0738411dbcedc5ad7d81304b"><span offset-key="9039bb1c0738411dbcedc5ad7d81304b:0">If there is an </span>`err`<span offset-key="9039bb1c0738411dbcedc5ad7d81304b:2"> object, it's better not to touch or rely on the </span>`result`<span offset-key="9039bb1c0738411dbcedc5ad7d81304b:4"> parameter.</span></span>

<span key="b30acc677f454b01a81ad0af5afd3c3f"><span offset-key="b30acc677f454b01a81ad0af5afd3c3f:0">Dealing with unhandled exceptions</span></span>

<span key="a9d13bb98a904a0cad0d6bce4c9f7768"><span offset-key="a9d13bb98a904a0cad0d6bce4c9f7768:0">=====-------------------------------------------------------------------</span></span>

<span key="4754b0457040411a8b7fa3c245c2a69c"><span offset-key="4754b0457040411a8b7fa3c245c2a69c:0">If your application uses third-party libraries, you have no control over how they deal with exceptions. There are cases when you might want to be able to deal with unhandled exceptions.</span></span>

## 

<span key="00e8c592104a45248812e34932e21c2c"><span offset-key="00e8c592104a45248812e34932e21c2c:0">Browser</span></span>

<span key="405fa8951dbb4f33be1083f8d28bd4da"><span offset-key="405fa8951dbb4f33be1083f8d28bd4da:0">Browsers expose a </span>`window.onerror`<span offset-key="405fa8951dbb4f33be1083f8d28bd4da:2"> event handler that can be used for this purpose.</span></span>

<span key="906cec8a22bd45738290729d0ff7db0c"><span offset-key="906cec8a22bd45738290729d0ff7db0c:0">Here is how you can use it:</span></span>

<span key="ec21460a380344498f9f38454c72aeb6"><span offset-key="ec21460a380344498f9f38454c72aeb6:0">This is what the arguments mean:</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="fcf9ca8388264d15a2c18772bef87193"><span offset-key="fcf9ca8388264d15a2c18772bef87193:0">msg --- The message associated with the error, e.g. </span>`Uncaught ReferenceError: foo is not defined`<span offset-key="fcf9ca8388264d15a2c18772bef87193:2">.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="c204bbc3f1c74989987237a86c62e692"><span offset-key="c204bbc3f1c74989987237a86c62e692:0">url --- The URL of the script or document associated with the error.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="46022bd95bb84895b6175b426fceeb10"><span offset-key="46022bd95bb84895b6175b426fceeb10:0">lineNo --- The line number (if available).</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="bd3375ffc2f74ff1be44f33e78b84919"><span offset-key="bd3375ffc2f74ff1be44f33e78b84919:0">columnNo --- The column number (if available).</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="db287880968446eb8dcc085f1d4cae1f"><span offset-key="db287880968446eb8dcc085f1d4cae1f:0">err --- The Error object associated with this error (if available).</span></span>

<span key="4cae9c482cec4cb7b8a4fffd0916cd9d"><span offset-key="4cae9c482cec4cb7b8a4fffd0916cd9d:0">When the function returns true, this prevents the firing of the default event handler.</span></span>

<span key="1e4becd9df234cae92a11e649b70785a"><span offset-key="1e4becd9df234cae92a11e649b70785a:0">There can be only one event handler assigned to </span>`window.onerror`<span offset-key="1e4becd9df234cae92a11e649b70785a:2"> because it is a function assignment, and there can only be one function assigned to an event at a time.</span></span>

<span key="69cb45750bb54bf7aa1060e50c17183b"><span offset-key="69cb45750bb54bf7aa1060e50c17183b:0">This means that if you assign your own </span>`window.onerror`<span offset-key="69cb45750bb54bf7aa1060e50c17183b:2">, you will override any previous handler that might have been assigned by third-party libraries. This can be a huge problem, especially for tools such as error trackers, as they will most likely completely stop working.</span></span>

<span key="01ad3c12677c40f781c120d1abe068c6"><span offset-key="01ad3c12677c40f781c120d1abe068c6:0">You can easily work around this problem by using the following trick:</span></span>

<span key="9d48d901037141dcb6f95f833d444346"><span offset-key="9d48d901037141dcb6f95f833d444346:0">Тhe code above checks if there was a previously defined </span>`window.onerror`<span offset-key="9d48d901037141dcb6f95f833d444346:2">, and simply calls it before proceeding. Using this pattern, you can keep adding additional handlers to </span>`window.onerror`<span offset-key="9d48d901037141dcb6f95f833d444346:4">.</span></span>

<span key="cae75860b4b0428d8ae90ce674d68ab7"><span offset-key="cae75860b4b0428d8ae90ce674d68ab7:0">This approach is highly compatible across browsers (it is supported even in IE6).</span></span>

<span key="10e6b0df568b4593b41adf0f6adecdb9"><span offset-key="10e6b0df568b4593b41adf0f6adecdb9:0">An alternative, which doesn't require replacing handlers, is adding an event listener to the </span>`window`<span offset-key="10e6b0df568b4593b41adf0f6adecdb9:2"> object:</span></span>

<span key="63e44711ea2b417c80b5cdbe6fb84089"><span offset-key="63e44711ea2b417c80b5cdbe6fb84089:0">This approach is much better, and also widely supported (from IE9 onwards).</span></span>

## 

<span key="02f6c6cd27004e52bfdd8a687cadf574"><span offset-key="02f6c6cd27004e52bfdd8a687cadf574:0">Node.js</span></span>

<span key="ec51df0677a143b2a2b0f50e4c623c1a"><span offset-key="ec51df0677a143b2a2b0f50e4c623c1a:0">The </span>`process`<span offset-key="ec51df0677a143b2a2b0f50e4c623c1a:2"> object from the </span>`EventEmmiter`<span offset-key="ec51df0677a143b2a2b0f50e4c623c1a:4"> module provides two events for handling errors.</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="1bdba6408473433880cd9666dd072f39">`uncaughtException`<span offset-key="1bdba6408473433880cd9666dd072f39:1"> --- emitted when an uncaught exception bubbles all the way back to the </span></span><a href="https://blog.sessionstack.com/how-javascript-works-event-loop-and-the-rise-of-async-programming-5-ways-to-better-coding-with-2f077c4438b5" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f504ae61011d4de38fa3051a5fbe4fd5" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="775a133625fc4a0a855f75dcc0e53896"><span data-offset-key="775a133625fc4a0a855f75dcc0e53896:0">event loop</span></span></span></a><span key="69b3e7adb421480eb885f06710602b16"><span offset-key="69b3e7adb421480eb885f06710602b16:0">. By default, Node.js handles such exceptions by printing the stack trace to stderr and exiting with </span>`code 1`<span offset-key="69b3e7adb421480eb885f06710602b16:2">. Adding a handler for this event overrides the default behavior. The correct use of the event is to perform synchronous cleanup of allocated resources (e.g. file descriptors, handles, etc) before shutting down the process. It is not safe to resume normal operation afterwards.</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="2fbcb093c2a54187b17cdf514b7510c4">`unhandledRejection`<span offset-key="2fbcb093c2a54187b17cdf514b7510c4:1"> --- emitted whenever a </span>`Promise`<span offset-key="2fbcb093c2a54187b17cdf514b7510c4:3"> is rejected and no error handler is attached to the promise within a turn of the </span></span><a href="https://blog.sessionstack.com/how-javascript-works-event-loop-and-the-rise-of-async-programming-5-ways-to-better-coding-with-2f077c4438b5" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="d7dae40b8b904e7ea29a7c0c889144b9" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="c2d76fca095646caac73eebeb2c9aefd"><span data-offset-key="c2d76fca095646caac73eebeb2c9aefd:0">event loop</span></span></span></a><span key="47c4cc78800140c481da449d8ef05231"><span offset-key="47c4cc78800140c481da449d8ef05231:0">. The </span>`unhandledRejection`<span offset-key="47c4cc78800140c481da449d8ef05231:2"> event is useful for detecting and keeping track of promises that were rejected and which rejections have not yet been handled.</span></span>

<span key="2e37260e25eb4e019c2a135258ca490b"><span offset-key="2e37260e25eb4e019c2a135258ca490b:0">It's really important that error handling is properly taken care of within your code. It's equally important to understand unhandled errors so that you can prioritize and work on them accordingly.</span></span>

<span key="b458b97301c64fdebe272ebb587d0874"><span offset-key="b458b97301c64fdebe272ebb587d0874:0">You can do this on your own, which can be quite tricky due to the wide variety of browsers, and all of the different cases that need to be taken care of. Alternatively, you can use some third-party tool to do this for you. No matter what option you choose, it's very important that you have as much information as possible about the error and the user context on how the error was triggered so that you can easily replicate it.</span></span>

<span key="ecaa38d0e6e548418677b31dda6da092"><span offset-key="ecaa38d0e6e548418677b31dda6da092:0">SessionStack is a solution that lets you replay JavaScript errors as if they happened in your browser. You can visually replay the exact user steps that led to the error, see the device, resolution, network, and all of the data that might be needed to connect the dots.</span></span>

# 

<span key="7fb9770fb14841a39b4fea14b7901406">**Flashcards**</span>

## 

<span key="3d78086063bb474c90ae0d5dda46be85">**Asynchronous**</span>

<span key="06f6ba73be404d7c96fec30742420957">**1. What are the arguments that the** **`setTimeout`** **and** **`setInterval`** **methods can accept?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="e24d8f90ffd6480ea9ca492c072573be"><span offset-key="e24d8f90ffd6480ea9ca492c072573be:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

    1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
        <span key="a000b7fdd51740319be799988d9ca1c1"><span offset-key="a000b7fdd51740319be799988d9ca1c1:0">a callback function</span></span>

    2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
        <span key="13cb5b491ebd475fa3e7fba252748d0f"><span offset-key="13cb5b491ebd475fa3e7fba252748d0f:0">a delay time in milliseconds</span></span>

    3.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">3.</span>
        <span key="d56b069b29424b579aaaa0d63d4a6509"><span offset-key="d56b069b29424b579aaaa0d63d4a6509:0">any number of additional arguments to be passed to the callback</span></span>

<span key="800e9c5c89fb4ca59b8765e42920a2df">**2. What does the** **`setTimeout`** **method return in the Node environment?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="b8f3520a08d847e3adad6ee266c2d059"><span offset-key="b8f3520a08d847e3adad6ee266c2d059:0">The </span>`setTimeout`<span offset-key="b8f3520a08d847e3adad6ee266c2d059:2"> method returns a Timeout object that can be passed to </span>`clearTimeout`<span offset-key="b8f3520a08d847e3adad6ee266c2d059:4"> to cancel the timeout.</span></span>

<span key="2bc2c457109f4a459cf0ccb79df4e6c3">**3. What does the** **`setTimeout`** **method return in the browser environment?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="56e80c43def54b0b992f80e69801f7d8"><span offset-key="56e80c43def54b0b992f80e69801f7d8:0">The </span>`setTimeout`<span offset-key="56e80c43def54b0b992f80e69801f7d8:2"> method returns a number representing the unique ID associated with that timeout. The ID number can be passed to </span>`clearTimeout`<span offset-key="56e80c43def54b0b992f80e69801f7d8:4"> to cancel the callback from running.</span></span>

<span key="b1b46cecdc134d4bb8a7bae74d1dbda7">**4. Is JavaScript single-threaded or multi-threaded?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="ae6812203d0545a6bbb3d95816af006f"><span offset-key="ae6812203d0545a6bbb3d95816af006f:0">Single-threaded.</span></span>

<span key="8b7c0acbb488483a91d3c0f3e7ef2262">**5. What is the difference between single-threaded and multi-threaded execution?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="a3c2285bb1a54173b82548932d3a301c"><span offset-key="a3c2285bb1a54173b82548932d3a301c:0">Single-threaded execution means that only one command can be processed at a time. In multi-threaded execution, more than one command can be processed at a time.</span></span>

<span key="e6f0642f7cf04c8a8adebd13ae603932">**6. What are the two main data structures that comprise JavaScript's event loop?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="1e71f77ce15249069a9b4c00bdf557f5"><span offset-key="1e71f77ce15249069a9b4c00bdf557f5:0">The call stack and event queue.</span></span>

<span key="001604831a1d45539145a60effb7f078">**7. When a function is called, what occurs on the call stack?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="3cba355004684138bfa2170711429e9e"><span offset-key="3cba355004684138bfa2170711429e9e:0">A new stack frame that corresponds to that function call is pushed to the top of the stack.</span></span>

<span key="56e24829715643f382a9adc9080ec237">**8. When a function returns, what occurs on the call stack?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="7d8aa5063b294df5a6c18ba345d95995"><span offset-key="7d8aa5063b294df5a6c18ba345d95995:0">The stack frame on top will be popped from the stack.</span></span>

<span key="d9f22a8a766d44b3994e26b3e6d5afd4">**9. In the JavaScript event loop, what is the message queue used for?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="3aab43883f1040949d2b24bc86a61521"><span offset-key="3aab43883f1040949d2b24bc86a61521:0">The message queue is used to track events that have occured but cannot be processed yet because the stack is already busy processing other commands. Once the stack is available, the "message" or event handler that is at the front of the queue will be moved to the stack for evaluation.</span></span>

<span key="c2c5a1dc48d94f64910378f3bd31baf5">**10. When an event triggers, what occurs in the JavaScript runtime's message queue?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="ba0281c5214d4a8c826d21533a4755b7"><span offset-key="ba0281c5214d4a8c826d21533a4755b7:0">A new message that corresponds to that event is enqueued (added to the back of the queue).</span></span>

<span key="3974f851ce204dd59fcdc38a1d39e07c">**11. In what order will the following code print to the console?**</span>

1

<span key="abc3a108784f42b5a9b65410a8165c9d"><span offset-key="abc3a108784f42b5a9b65410a8165c9d:0">console.log("first");</span></span>

2

<span key="3928b513d7654ee2b601e9ee3385d2f6"><span offset-key="3928b513d7654ee2b601e9ee3385d2f6:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

3

<span key="dc4a5593c4ea45e9944de4528e8015c2"><span offset-key="dc4a5593c4ea45e9944de4528e8015c2:0">setTimeout(function () {</span></span>

<span key="7246ac238f194d50a2a117249a7d5e1f"><span offset-key="7246ac238f194d50a2a117249a7d5e1f:0"> console.log("second");</span></span>

<span key="2f4e50358f7a472893805e68063174fd">**12. What must occur for items to be dequeued (removed) from the JavaScript runtime's message queue?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="f89bc3df10554e489213afe574826061"><span offset-key="f89bc3df10554e489213afe574826061:0">The call stack must become empty. This happens when current task is finished executing.</span></span>

<span key="46447f2573154009826891587142fd5d">**13. What is the difference between synchronous and asynchronous code?**</span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJoZWlnaHQ6MTJweDt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm r-1vzi8xi" />

    <span key="cd557d187901425392da4cdeb8784462"><span offset-key="cd557d187901425392da4cdeb8784462:0">In synchronous code, the commands execute one after the other in order. This means that completion of a "slow" function will block execution of further functions. In asynchronous code, the commands are not guaranteed to occur one after the other; an asynchronous function will not block execution of further functions.</span></span>

## 

<span key="5a9429487b11449495fadee2475f9408"><span offset-key="5a9429487b11449495fadee2475f9408:0">2. Abstract Test Assertions into a JavaScript Assertion Library</span></span>

<span key="1ec5f3d26bb644ff88b8317cc0076805"><span offset-key="1ec5f3d26bb644ff88b8317cc0076805:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/02-abstract-assertions.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="71c9e114515942709908062fea818142" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="8c22f542027048b6827fea3aad772549"><span data-offset-key="8c22f542027048b6827fea3aad772549:0">02-abstract-assertions.js</span></span></span></a><span key="87755d4bf4dc4cd1a0265603a188de5c"><span offset-key="87755d4bf4dc4cd1a0265603a188de5c:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>

<span key="ddcf914a3eb747aeb20e4531a3da50d0"><span offset-key="ddcf914a3eb747aeb20e4531a3da50d0:0">An assertion library can be as simple as a function which takes a result and returns an object containing a number of different assertions which allows the user to determine how they want to evaluate that result against an expected value.</span></span>

## 

<span key="920dfe5afc514df0896b797e902402bc"><span offset-key="920dfe5afc514df0896b797e902402bc:0">3. Encapsulate and Isolate Tests by building a JavaScript Testing Framework</span></span>

<span key="3d8fe09d383344d280453627c8e287ef"><span offset-key="3d8fe09d383344d280453627c8e287ef:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/03-encapsulate-and-isolate-tests.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="8f5d078a47a849929a36a992fbeae0bd" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="44b5a45525d54c7b948a53b7ed26b00b"><span data-offset-key="44b5a45525d54c7b948a53b7ed26b00b:0">03-encapsulate-and-isolate-tests.js</span></span></span></a><span key="c174426846544ea1897fed7070860d49"><span offset-key="c174426846544ea1897fed7070860d49:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>
