## 

<span key="b5656b7fb5b547e09fa54b8f0e27ccd6"><span offset-key="b5656b7fb5b547e09fa54b8f0e27ccd6:0">6. Avoid Common Errors with Flow Type Definitions</span></span>

<span key="d6702acbad94492fafe595f8a2e42ac0"><span offset-key="d6702acbad94492fafe595f8a2e42ac0:0">Use </span>`@flow`<span offset-key="d6702acbad94492fafe595f8a2e42ac0:2"> at the top of files that you want to use </span>`flow`<span offset-key="d6702acbad94492fafe595f8a2e42ac0:4"> to make type strict after installing </span>`flow-bin`<span offset-key="d6702acbad94492fafe595f8a2e42ac0:6"> as a dev dependency.</span></span>

## 

<span key="af02065391b54df0aad23d3a631ce40d"><span offset-key="af02065391b54df0aad23d3a631ce40d:0">7. Validate Code in a pre-commit git Hook with husky</span></span>

<span key="ee3f55ebbfc74317abd4de705a1a0f0f">`husky`<span offset-key="ee3f55ebbfc74317abd4de705a1a0f0f:1"> works in a similar way to </span>`ghooks`<span offset-key="ee3f55ebbfc74317abd4de705a1a0f0f:3">, except that you add npm scripts to run pre and post-hooks.</span></span>

## 

<span key="10e9d974295144b3a4043733d6fbe124"><span offset-key="10e9d974295144b3a4043733d6fbe124:0">8. Auto-format all files and validate relevant files in a precommit script with </span>`lint-staged`</span>

<span key="eb899be3663642b8b8610bb9890261eb">`lint-staged`<span offset-key="eb899be3663642b8b8610bb9890261eb:1"> not only allows linters to be run on precommit, but allows one to define commands to be run should linting pass, allowing for repo owners to have autoformatting run and changed files staged without relying on collaborators to have autoformatters enabled.</span></span>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHByZXNlcnZlYXNwZWN0cmF0aW89InhNaWRZTWlkIG1lZXQiIGRhdGEtcm53LWludC1jbGFzcz0ibmVhcmVzdF9fXzU3OC0yNjgyXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIHItMTBwdHVuNyByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJ3aWR0aDoxNnB4Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTAgLjVBLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUgMGgxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEuNS41VjRoLTFWMUgxdjloM3YxSC41YS41LjUgMCAwMS0uNS0uNVYuNXoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjxwYXRoIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xpcC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIiBkPSJNNSA1LjVhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUtLjVoMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUuNXYxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEtLjUuNWgtMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLS41LS41di0xMHpNNiA2djloOVY2SDZ6IiBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiPjwvcGF0aD48L3N2Zz4=" class="r-h7gdob r-10ptun7 r-1vzi8xi" />

Copied!

<span key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7"><span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:0">We import both </span>`thumb-war`<span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:2"> and </span>`utils`<span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:4">, and mock out </span>`utils.getWinner`<span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:6"> so that we can evaluate other aspects of </span>`thumb-war`<span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:8">. We are making </span>`utils.getWinner`<span offset-key="5a3b6c3ae1794552ade65626340a5ad7:10"> deterministic, as the randomness of what it usually returns will affect the outcomes of our tests in non-deterministic ways.</span></span>

<span key="9da575c23a844062a9defd6f787148d0"><span offset-key="9da575c23a844062a9defd6f787148d0:0">After mocking, one should always clean up so that subsequent tests are not affected by the mock.</span></span>

## 

<span key="861f49ab5ceb4a069db7089e1dc4df94"><span offset-key="861f49ab5ceb4a069db7089e1dc4df94:0">2. Ensure Functions are Called Correctly with JavaScript Mocks</span></span>

<span key="0549d2e2b1114193a159ccd2c98f0e84"><span offset-key="0549d2e2b1114193a159ccd2c98f0e84:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/02-ensure-functions-are-called-correctly-with-javascript-mocks.test.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="0b135ab4a58b40ed9a29ee67e2bc957e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="69f984c3edfa46b88d9a7f9ef096dbb9"><span data-offset-key="69f984c3edfa46b88d9a7f9ef096dbb9:0">02-ensure-functions-are-called-correctly-with-javascript-mocks.test.js</span></span></span></a><span key="0fc931a2e99a476bbb2e314ad5f05ba1"><span offset-key="0fc931a2e99a476bbb2e314ad5f05ba1:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>

<span key="ffdf1581855f40c3b1ee2c667dc04a32"><span offset-key="ffdf1581855f40c3b1ee2c667dc04a32:0">$ npx jest 02</span></span>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHByZXNlcnZlYXNwZWN0cmF0aW89InhNaWRZTWlkIG1lZXQiIGRhdGEtcm53LWludC1jbGFzcz0ibmVhcmVzdF9fXzU3OC0yNjgyXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIHItMTBwdHVuNyByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJ3aWR0aDoxNnB4Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTAgLjVBLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUgMGgxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEuNS41VjRoLTFWMUgxdjloM3YxSC41YS41LjUgMCAwMS0uNS0uNVYuNXoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjxwYXRoIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xpcC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIiBkPSJNNSA1LjVhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUtLjVoMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUuNXYxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEtLjUuNWgtMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLS41LS41di0xMHpNNiA2djloOVY2SDZ6IiBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiPjwvcGF0aD48L3N2Zz4=" class="r-h7gdob r-10ptun7 r-1vzi8xi" />

Copied!

<span key="7d2472dc520c47b99ae92d8d4b4217c8"><span offset-key="7d2472dc520c47b99ae92d8d4b4217c8:0">We can create a naive </span>`jest.fn`<span offset-key="7d2472dc520c47b99ae92d8d4b4217c8:2"> which takes a mock implementation, and accepts all arguments passed to it.</span></span>

<span key="a95684eb59964d669fc1a95de3b96e27"><span offset-key="a95684eb59964d669fc1a95de3b96e27:0">Onto this mock function we can add a </span>`mock`<span offset-key="a95684eb59964d669fc1a95de3b96e27:2"> object where we can store calls to the mock function.</span></span>

<span key="3bd7dba217fa434b8cbf0b26ef424255"><span offset-key="3bd7dba217fa434b8cbf0b26ef424255:0">This can all be done using </span>`jest.fn`<span offset-key="3bd7dba217fa434b8cbf0b26ef424255:2">.</span></span>

<span key="54287d3a36dd4b64849b68e48f6cb50f"><span offset-key="54287d3a36dd4b64849b68e48f6cb50f:0">Jest allows one to inspect a mocked function using </span>`toHaveBeenCalledWith`<span offset-key="54287d3a36dd4b64849b68e48f6cb50f:2">, </span>`toHaveBeenNthCalledWith`<span offset-key="54287d3a36dd4b64849b68e48f6cb50f:4">, or to inspect </span>`mockFn.mock.calls`<span offset-key="54287d3a36dd4b64849b68e48f6cb50f:6"> to inspect how the function was used for all calls.</span></span>

## 

<span key="dedc41345f89411bb2847fadbaa54a65"><span offset-key="dedc41345f89411bb2847fadbaa54a65:0">3. Restore the Original Implementation of a Mocked JavaScript Function with jest.spyOn</span></span>

<span key="d22431a7ec444b0abe984580bbc0226a"><span offset-key="d22431a7ec444b0abe984580bbc0226a:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/03-restore-original-implementation-of-a-mocked-function.test.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="93d18ce7683c4b6a95876a4de6b92cae" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="40ee9b4edc324131896d3fbeaf867438"><span data-offset-key="40ee9b4edc324131896d3fbeaf867438:0">03-restore-original-implementation-of-a-mocked-function.test.js</span></span></span></a><span key="97f3f004f1cf40b6bcad440862b77ace"><span offset-key="97f3f004f1cf40b6bcad440862b77ace:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>

6

<span key="078098ed30b44e9eb1468b9463ecd8b1"><span offset-key="078098ed30b44e9eb1468b9463ecd8b1:0">$ node 03-restore-original-implementation-of-a-mocked-function.no-framework.js</span></span>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHByZXNlcnZlYXNwZWN0cmF0aW89InhNaWRZTWlkIG1lZXQiIGRhdGEtcm53LWludC1jbGFzcz0ibmVhcmVzdF9fXzU3OC0yNjgyXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIHItMTBwdHVuNyByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJ3aWR0aDoxNnB4Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTAgLjVBLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUgMGgxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEuNS41VjRoLTFWMUgxdjloM3YxSC41YS41LjUgMCAwMS0uNS0uNVYuNXoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjxwYXRoIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xpcC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIiBkPSJNNSA1LjVhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUtLjVoMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUuNXYxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEtLjUuNWgtMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLS41LS41di0xMHpNNiA2djloOVY2SDZ6IiBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiPjwvcGF0aD48L3N2Zz4=" class="r-h7gdob r-10ptun7 r-1vzi8xi" />

Copied!

<span key="ddfad489f1a6485bba0991d28405342e"><span offset-key="ddfad489f1a6485bba0991d28405342e:0">An alternative to using jest.fn to replace a function with a mock implementation is to use </span>`jest.spyOn`<span offset-key="ddfad489f1a6485bba0991d28405342e:2"> to create a mock implementation. This mitigates us having to store the original function and replace it, as Jest will do the heavy lifting for us.</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="7168ce9a2f5244fd8b77e28d980ed8f7"><span offset-key="7168ce9a2f5244fd8b77e28d980ed8f7:0">Use </span>`jest.spyOn(myObject, 'myObjectFn')`</span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="687abc524528429ca9aec2330243602f"><span offset-key="687abc524528429ca9aec2330243602f:0">Use </span>`myObject.myObjectFn.mockImplementation(mockFn)`<span offset-key="687abc524528429ca9aec2330243602f:2"> to create a mock implementation of </span>`myObjectFn`</span>

3.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">3.</span>
    <span key="7bbcdf3ccafb4799a38f0253af4b8e79"><span offset-key="7bbcdf3ccafb4799a38f0253af4b8e79:0">Once done testing the implementation, use </span>`myObject.myObjectFn.mockRestore()`<span offset-key="7bbcdf3ccafb4799a38f0253af4b8e79:2"> to replace the mock implementation with the original so that other tests are not affected. </span>`.mockRestore()`<span offset-key="7bbcdf3ccafb4799a38f0253af4b8e79:4"> restores the mock implementation to its pre-mocked definition</span></span>

## 

<span key="fbe3325c0ff24242ba21768d43e3eacc"><span offset-key="fbe3325c0ff24242ba21768d43e3eacc:0">4. Mock a JavaScript module in a test</span></span>

<span key="b507aa4f9d784b2f9ccc285f247c1497"><span offset-key="b507aa4f9d784b2f9ccc285f247c1497:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/04-mock-a-js-module-in-a-test.test.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f24f9ddfa0a64201a9e8cfefcaf22bb9" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="58de70facf01470f9e193b724c822780"><span data-offset-key="58de70facf01470f9e193b724c822780:0">04-mock-a-js-module-in-a-test.test.js</span></span></span></a><span key="4ceddb31c0d24ebb9daad979df74dd8f"><span offset-key="4ceddb31c0d24ebb9daad979df74dd8f:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>

<span key="429650b06f4542b08ba9c21fb038fa3f"><span offset-key="429650b06f4542b08ba9c21fb038fa3f:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

5

<span key="eb02d1063a4141fa9a3a0cb1ce751db3"><span offset-key="eb02d1063a4141fa9a3a0cb1ce751db3:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

6

<span key="a57c179cbd2245a1996beabe44a30135"><span offset-key="a57c179cbd2245a1996beabe44a30135:0">$ node 04-mock-a-js-module-in-a-test.no-framework.js</span></span>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGZpbGw9Im5vbmUiIHByZXNlcnZlYXNwZWN0cmF0aW89InhNaWRZTWlkIG1lZXQiIGRhdGEtcm53LWludC1jbGFzcz0ibmVhcmVzdF9fXzU3OC0yNjgyXyIgY2xhc3M9InItaDdnZG9iIHItMTBwdHVuNyByLTF2emk4eGkiIHN0eWxlPSJ3aWR0aDoxNnB4Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsLXJ1bGU9ImV2ZW5vZGQiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTAgLjVBLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUgMGgxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEuNS41VjRoLTFWMUgxdjloM3YxSC41YS41LjUgMCAwMS0uNS0uNVYuNXoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciI+PC9wYXRoPjxwYXRoIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xpcC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIiBkPSJNNSA1LjVhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUtLjVoMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLjUuNXYxMGEuNS41IDAgMDEtLjUuNWgtMTBhLjUuNSAwIDAxLS41LS41di0xMHpNNiA2djloOVY2SDZ6IiBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiPjwvcGF0aD48L3N2Zz4=" class="r-h7gdob r-10ptun7 r-1vzi8xi" />

Copied!

<span key="43074045f1f84fe09bd1874fae16a8a6"><span offset-key="43074045f1f84fe09bd1874fae16a8a6:0">Using </span>`jest.spyOn`<span offset-key="43074045f1f84fe09bd1874fae16a8a6:2"> is still a form of monkey-patching. Monkey-patching is great for our own modules, because we're using commonjs's </span>`require`<span offset-key="43074045f1f84fe09bd1874fae16a8a6:4">. When working in an es environment we'll have to mock an entire module, and </span>`jest.mock`<span offset-key="43074045f1f84fe09bd1874fae16a8a6:6"> allows one to do this.</span></span>

<span key="f496a8d305ce4fa0961737a0a4275a71"><span offset-key="f496a8d305ce4fa0961737a0a4275a71:0">When using </span>`jest.mock`<span offset-key="f496a8d305ce4fa0961737a0a4275a71:2"> we can create the mock implementation inside of the mock, and no longer need to use </span>`jest.spyOn`<span offset-key="f496a8d305ce4fa0961737a0a4275a71:4"> and </span>`[fnToMock].mockImplementation`<span offset-key="f496a8d305ce4fa0961737a0a4275a71:6">.</span></span>

<span key="0ac93ad3a9044d17b4f31065d6cfbbff"><span offset-key="0ac93ad3a9044d17b4f31065d6cfbbff:0">Instead of using </span>`mock.mockRestore()`<span offset-key="0ac93ad3a9044d17b4f31065d6cfbbff:2"> to restore the mock implementation, we now use </span>`mock.mockReset()`<span offset-key="0ac93ad3a9044d17b4f31065d6cfbbff:4">. </span>`mock.mockRestore()`<span offset-key="0ac93ad3a9044d17b4f31065d6cfbbff:6"> is only available for mocks created with </span>`jest.spyOn`</span>

<span key="5a9900afb9a44f11a0c8be978bc9d02e">`jest.mock`<span offset-key="5a9900afb9a44f11a0c8be978bc9d02e:1"> can be placed anywhere in the file, and Jest will hoist it to the top of the file.</span></span>

<span key="ea84603be676462bb4488eb819da94c0"><span offset-key="ea84603be676462bb4488eb819da94c0:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

<span key="8349a501fb8f4d1cad426fa92451dff3">`jest.mock`<span offset-key="8349a501fb8f4d1cad426fa92451dff3:1"> takes control of the entire module requiring system. This can be simulated using </span>`require.cache`<span offset-key="8349a501fb8f4d1cad426fa92451dff3:3">. </span>`require.cache`<span offset-key="8349a501fb8f4d1cad426fa92451dff3:5"> is an object that has keys for each import, with each key being associated with an object containining information regarding the import.</span></span>

<span key="bffa43568c4644cba154b8a74d4d6156"><span offset-key="bffa43568c4644cba154b8a74d4d6156:0">We use the </span>`exports`<span offset-key="bffa43568c4644cba154b8a74d4d6156:2"> property to create the mock implementation of the module</span></span>

## 

<span key="ef8a4978c6234a4ebb77085b501482b5"><span offset-key="ef8a4978c6234a4ebb77085b501482b5:0">5. Make a shared JavaScript mock module</span></span>

<span key="ea092338b03745abaedac9b3762d4bb7"><span offset-key="ea092338b03745abaedac9b3762d4bb7:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="file:///C:/Users/bryan/Downloads/05-make-a-shared-mock-module.test.js" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="47425f4978f040a5bca7cf90f4587b1c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="a38f7afed575450db17199a31d4d7b56"><span data-offset-key="a38f7afed575450db17199a31d4d7b56:0">05-make-a-shared-mock-module.test.js</span></span></span></a><span key="8a78b1fb19f54038a138e6b2a7708676"><span offset-key="8a78b1fb19f54038a138e6b2a7708676:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span>

1

<span key="d02fdc71994343d5991faf760b961ed6"><span offset-key="d02fdc71994343d5991faf760b961ed6:0">$ npx jest 05</span></span>

2

<span key="abb4f818f27e49e4ba742b41cd31ac29"><span offset-key="abb4f818f27e49e4ba742b41cd31ac29:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

3

<span key="4afc2a28a4694d469ae10dbe989645c6"><span offset-key="4afc2a28a4694d469ae10dbe989645c6:0"># or</span></span>

4

<span key="c8ca138bb1c145b4b63578f9d7cc0c99"><span offset-key="c8ca138bb1c145b4b63578f9d7cc0c99:0">$ node 05-make-a-shared-mock-module.no-framework.js</span></span>

Copied!

<span key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05"><span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:0">We can have tests automatically use the mock of a module by adding the mock to a </span>`__mocks__`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:2"> folder. Node modules can be placed in the </span>`root`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:4"> </span>`__mocks__`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:6"> that Jest inspects, by default adjacent to </span>`node_modules`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:8">. For user-defined </span>`modules`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:10"> they can be placed in a </span>`__mocks__`<span offset-key="87b106542f9744f3b06cb0acc62f7c05:12"> folder adjacent to the module. The mock must use the same filename as the mocked module.</span></span>

<span key="85aa66b448e34d03988f0b6967d35ba7"><span offset-key="85aa66b448e34d03988f0b6967d35ba7:0">For user-defined modules, if the test imports the module, then </span>`jest.mock('./path/to/mock')`<span offset-key="85aa66b448e34d03988f0b6967d35ba7:2"> must be added to the test file.</span></span>

<span key="dc6d974328a748b89665ef2a5c8626b8"><span offset-key="dc6d974328a748b89665ef2a5c8626b8:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

<span key="eddabd4daccc4940a4ee21fd3ec7b7ef"><span offset-key="eddabd4daccc4940a4ee21fd3ec7b7ef:0">Similarly to how we simulated what Jest is doing when conrolling module requiring by using </span>`require.cache`<span offset-key="eddabd4daccc4940a4ee21fd3ec7b7ef:2">. We create a file containing the mock, which also uses our </span>`fn`<span offset-key="eddabd4daccc4940a4ee21fd3ec7b7ef:4"> to allow us to evaluate calls. In our test we import our mock, and then retrieve the cached paths for the actual utils and mock utils, rewriting </span>`require.cache`<span offset-key="eddabd4daccc4940a4ee21fd3ec7b7ef:6">'s key for the actual utils with the mocked utils.</span></span>

<span key="4c8bb778f5fc48a987b7597f9d8704a8"><span offset-key="4c8bb778f5fc48a987b7597f9d8704a8:0">Notes Node vs Browser A tale of Two Runtimes: Node.js vs Browser</span></span>

<span key="28f4af7bc0e843a6bde4b6c8cf170767"><span offset-key="28f4af7bc0e843a6bde4b6c8cf170767:0">Different browsers can differ wildly because JS is treated as a specification. Global vs Window</span></span>

<span key="7716c56924564708bcda79028e1292d1"><span offset-key="7716c56924564708bcda79028e1292d1:0">In Node.js runtime, global object is where global variables are stored.</span></span>

<span key="cb7e8e9dd42446a79d556720842f6193"><span offset-key="cb7e8e9dd42446a79d556720842f6193:0">In browsers, window objects are where global variables are stored.</span></span>

<span key="4db0aa682ab848c88075281e7c80f197"><span offset-key="4db0aa682ab848c88075281e7c80f197:0">We cannot reference window in node. Browsers have access to the document object, which contains the html for the page, node does not have this.</span></span>

<span key="3bc162f3434e4261aeb975ba352460d5"><span offset-key="3bc162f3434e4261aeb975ba352460d5:0">Browsers also have access to a location that contains information about the web address, node doesn't.</span></span>

<span key="57e5a4a913ba4ac99adadaa5a8ec5388"><span offset-key="57e5a4a913ba4ac99adadaa5a8ec5388:0">Node has the require module, that we can use to import installed modules, and export our own files.</span></span>

<span key="8ea002d68b1c4b7da31ced8356efd3f6"><span offset-key="8ea002d68b1c4b7da31ced8356efd3f6:0">File I/O The FS Module</span></span>

<span key="c54b89d199b74c4db16cf57c878cd633"><span offset-key="c54b89d199b74c4db16cf57c878cd633:0">Node ships with a File System module that contains methods that allow us to interact with our pc's FS.</span></span>

<span key="3a73b6dc7a094dc2bd78f5bd83221ee9"><span offset-key="3a73b6dc7a094dc2bd78f5bd83221ee9:0">require will return to us a object with many properties that will enable us to do file I/O.</span></span>

<span key="dbc35f293e3b46cbb1cc511010d182eb"><span offset-key="dbc35f293e3b46cbb1cc511010d182eb:0">The file system (fs) module contains a lot of functionality.</span></span>

<span key="b8ddfe06e5ae4132bd1909a29cf97e08"><span offset-key="b8ddfe06e5ae4132bd1909a29cf97e08:0">Offers both async and sync functions. Most likely covers all operations regarding files. Creating a New File</span></span>

<span key="5584bf4246e84b9696dd1d9c305f7020"><span offset-key="5584bf4246e84b9696dd1d9c305f7020:0">Write File : Method used to create an file in the FS module. fs.writeFile("foo.txt", "Hello world!", "utf8", (err) => { if (err) { console.log(err); } console.log("write is complete"); }); Arguments go as follows: Name of new file. String input. Code Encoding (UTF-8) Callback to signal end Since Write File is async, we need to use callback chaining to guarantee commands occur after a write completes or fails. Reading Existing Files</span></span>

<span key="2a581882f6114734b31845f18fc1b0fa"><span offset-key="2a581882f6114734b31845f18fc1b0fa:0">Read File : Method used to read the contents of a file. Arguments go as follows:</span></span>

<span key="8211a64343ac4b7399863a60dfadbd24"><span offset-key="8211a64343ac4b7399863a60dfadbd24:0">Name of new file.</span></span>

<span key="58bcfcb892f3416e8d5ed3c4af994eb7"><span offset-key="58bcfcb892f3416e8d5ed3c4af994eb7:0">Code Encoding (UTF-8)</span></span>

<span key="a1295ab619ea4441b574a0a198c28773"><span offset-key="a1295ab619ea4441b574a0a198c28773:0">Error Object</span></span>

<span key="23fe8b835d984e9faef7ad13d21f355f"><span offset-key="23fe8b835d984e9faef7ad13d21f355f:0">Callback to signal end</span></span>

<span key="7887c00a4a574e58a6e956c1cfa68536"><span offset-key="7887c00a4a574e58a6e956c1cfa68536:0">fs.readFile("poetry.txt", "utf8", (err, data) => { if (err) { console.log(err); } console.log("THE CONTENTS ARE:"); console.log(data); }); You can do anything you want with the contents of a read file, since it is just one giant string! Fancy File I/O</span></span>

<span key="0ffbe930ac534f229683183c6132c992"><span offset-key="0ffbe930ac534f229683183c6132c992:0">We can use Read File and Write file together to replace occurences of certain phrases with something else.</span></span>

<span key="0ade7232960447bbb0181675de37079d"><span offset-key="0ade7232960447bbb0181675de37079d:0">const fs = require("fs");</span></span>

<span key="3ac10ee464644e74b2e49d4d44c3e70a"><span offset-key="3ac10ee464644e74b2e49d4d44c3e70a:0">function replaceContents(file, oldStr, newStr) { fs.readFile(file, "utf8", (err, data) => { if (err) { console.log(err); } let newData = data.split(oldStr).join(newStr); writeContents(file, newData); }); }</span></span>

<span key="cdd56cdee868471b863a54943c8102ce"><span offset-key="cdd56cdee868471b863a54943c8102ce:0">function writeContents(file, data) { fs.writeFile(file, data, "utf8", (err) => { if (err) { console.log(err); } console.log("done!"); }); }</span></span>

<span key="f7c57f5efac5484aa4ec1e82f22d323f"><span offset-key="f7c57f5efac5484aa4ec1e82f22d323f:0">replaceContents("poetry.txt", "do not", "should"); Gitting Started with Git Version Control Systems help us keep track of changes over time.</span></span>

<span key="09e9b6c41d944910a93e95b8d2e624cb"><span offset-key="09e9b6c41d944910a93e95b8d2e624cb:0">VCS tools abstract the work of keeping projects and programmers in sync with one another. Git is the most popular VCS in use today.</span></span>

<span key="6f422f9a5c464dd3bc072fb24ea2a311"><span offset-key="6f422f9a5c464dd3bc072fb24ea2a311:0">Repository : Comprises all the source code for a particular project.</span></span>

<span key="a8fd5d2d47584b389f67499cadd5df70"><span offset-key="a8fd5d2d47584b389f67499cadd5df70:0">Commits : collection of changes grouped towards a shared purpose.</span></span>

<span key="bef3254a03d54e9fb3613ae0394a6745"><span offset-key="bef3254a03d54e9fb3613ae0394a6745:0">msg and hash</span></span>

<span key="323b3fea9eec46f6b5a4c4603027ff93"><span offset-key="323b3fea9eec46f6b5a4c4603027ff93:0">Commit Messages & Commit Hashes : Git id's your commits with a specially generated series of letters and numbers called a Hash, and a detailed message describing the commit.</span></span>

<span key="6f45e1f2c7b1489aa8ac9910c0b5c03e"><span offset-key="6f45e1f2c7b1489aa8ac9910c0b5c03e:0">They are 40 characters long, but by default Git abbreivates hashes to 7 characters. References : Way to alias a commit in plain english.</span></span>

<span key="2c37ba6ed1e54926b3020dce63cc5da2"><span offset-key="2c37ba6ed1e54926b3020dce63cc5da2:0">HEAD : default reference that points to the most recent commit. Git maintains three lists of changes:</span></span>

<span key="e59113018a144c0ea1c94429dc52a3a0"><span offset-key="e59113018a144c0ea1c94429dc52a3a0:0">Working Directory Keeps all of your in-progress changes. Staging Area Reserved for changes you're ready to commit. Commit History Made up of changes you've already committed. Tracking Changes in a Repository</span></span>

<span key="789f9c75c3a544aa858c7b01a17db43c"><span offset-key="789f9c75c3a544aa858c7b01a17db43c:0">Git Init : Allows you to start a repository in your current directory.</span></span>

<span key="adcc12d9e55b44a1913a2a8f3266e932"><span offset-key="adcc12d9e55b44a1913a2a8f3266e932:0">Git Add : Adds content to your repository.</span></span>

<span key="1de380ef487a4e5ebd5bd96d18dee543"><span offset-key="1de380ef487a4e5ebd5bd96d18dee543:0">Git Status : Used to check what has been staged in your repository.</span></span>

<span key="e9cb7850021f4e78aad50e78403984e9"><span offset-key="e9cb7850021f4e78aad50e78403984e9:0">Git Commit -m : Used to commit your changes/additions into the commit history - flag is used to add a message to your commit.</span></span>

<span key="bf4f9e8eee824261aa6d1366283ef5dc"><span offset-key="bf4f9e8eee824261aa6d1366283ef5dc:0">Git Log : Used to check your repo's commit history.</span></span>

<span key="da52474de1b64ce6bdc4a09d8143da6d"><span offset-key="da52474de1b64ce6bdc4a09d8143da6d:0">Branches and Workflow</span></span>

<span key="6d2ea14d0aea49f0a5cd157f52a0f582"><span offset-key="6d2ea14d0aea49f0a5cd157f52a0f582:0">Branch : Basically a seperate timeline in Git, reserved for it's own changes - Master is the default branch.</span></span>

<span key="2e535d2c32c247fdab96834056f643d5"><span offset-key="2e535d2c32c247fdab96834056f643d5:0">Git branch \[name of branch\] : Used to reate a new branch. img of branch</span></span>

<span key="d04b1845497444969780fdb2145035da"><span offset-key="d04b1845497444969780fdb2145035da:0">Git Checkout : Used to switch to an existing branch.</span></span>

<span key="572d8381c2ef43b9a96211870553c0b5"><span offset-key="572d8381c2ef43b9a96211870553c0b5:0">Bringing it Back Together</span></span>

<span key="4256ee9b15be4d73875300cdafbe9176"><span offset-key="4256ee9b15be4d73875300cdafbe9176:0">Git Merge : Used to integrate one branch into another. Connecting with the world via Github</span></span>

<span key="0267ba9371494b46b275f84e07ab8087"><span offset-key="0267ba9371494b46b275f84e07ab8087:0">DCVS : Distributed Version Control System - built in support for managing code both locally and from a distant source.</span></span>

<span key="a359c7dcd3154ef8b67420435bc2331e"><span offset-key="a359c7dcd3154ef8b67420435bc2331e:0">We typically refer to the primary remote of a repo as the origin.</span></span>

<span key="c6d4edc509d948bf95d522baef1659a7"><span offset-key="c6d4edc509d948bf95d522baef1659a7:0">We clone a distant repo once, use pull to update it and push our own code into it.</span></span>

<span key="0bd6c1eb9d28410fa20607aa03dc82db"><span offset-key="0bd6c1eb9d28410fa20607aa03dc82db:0">Collaboration via Git and Github</span></span>

> <span key="25c1bf61f4314a57b8815873a7a01ddf"><span offset-key="25c1bf61f4314a57b8815873a7a01ddf:0">git branch add-my-new-file git add my-new-file.js git commit -m "Add new file" git push -u origin add-my-new-file This is the typical push workflow.</span></span>

<span key="99972abd10b54c1ba3f52808a194856d"><span offset-key="99972abd10b54c1ba3f52808a194856d:0">-u flag stands for --set-upstream.</span></span>

<span key="8e4570daccfe4ff4946a71bdfca01a3e"><span offset-key="8e4570daccfe4ff4946a71bdfca01a3e:0">Git Pull : Used to update your files from remote repo - behind the scenes this is a combination of Git Fetch and Git Merge. git pull behind</span></span>

<span key="9c0c52dcd41d4d85956cb528448c3109"><span offset-key="9c0c52dcd41d4d85956cb528448c3109:0">Pull Request : Feature specific to Github, used as a safety net to prevent bugs and is a critical aspect of collaboration workflow.</span></span>

<span key="0ef75285f607465b96b8b899d50d784d"><span offset-key="0ef75285f607465b96b8b899d50d784d:0">Push your code to GH on it's own branch. Open pull request via a base branch. GH creates a comparison page for your new code vs existing. Your teammates review for errors. Make changes based on feedback and push new commits upwards. PR automatically makes changes. If everyone is satisfied, a repo maintainer will merge your branch. Your code is now on the main branch - nice! Managing your Github Repository Git Diff : Used to visualize any tracked differences in our repository. img of diff --- & +++ : let's us know there are both additions & subtractions in our js file. @@ : shows use where our chunk of changes are line-wise. Diff Options</span></span>

<span key="463869a6962046a48113fc5e586f0f98"><span offset-key="463869a6962046a48113fc5e586f0f98:0">By default git diff compares the cwd to the last commit. If we append --staged we can compare the staging area instead of the cwd. There are many other ways to use git diff to compare as well!</span></span>

# 

<span key="2d9f4256dec644fab530b1e2a255683f"><span offset-key="2d9f4256dec644fab530b1e2a255683f:0">You can use "HEAD~N" to move N commits prior</span></span>

# 

<span key="64a866520a6e4b749d915191589f7b30"><span offset-key="64a866520a6e4b749d915191589f7b30:0">to the current HEAD</span></span>

> <span key="cf14f27138084067819ae6734629109f"><span offset-key="cf14f27138084067819ae6734629109f:0">git checkout HEAD~3 Git Do-over: Reset and Rebase Git Reset : Can be used to travel back in time before a bug or error occured. --soft : appended to reset to move our HEAD ref to the commit we specified - does not touch our code, only resets commit messages.(least dangerous!) --mixed : Default state of Git reset, changes are preserved but they are removed from the commit history straight to the working directory. --hard : Adjust head ref and totally destroy any interim code changes Rebase: An Alternative Form of Time Travel</span></span>

<span key="92efe1d25d72458e95aca7d3796e2f2a"><span offset-key="92efe1d25d72458e95aca7d3796e2f2a:0">Git Rebase : Involves changing your current branch's base branch. Rebasing is a dangerous process that involves re-writing history. diagram of rebase The Golden Rule of Git</span></span>

<span key="b653af67f6c94b1388f5839ca9332581"><span offset-key="b653af67f6c94b1388f5839ca9332581:0">Never change the history of a branch that's shared with others.</span></span>

<span key="783d127c0c15442992678d4e98cfa716"><span offset-key="783d127c0c15442992678d4e98cfa716:0">This rule refers to git reset and git rebase. Just don't use these on any branch that is shared with others!!! Git Merge Conflicts & You Merge Conflict : Special state that Git presents to us when two branches have code changes that are incompatible with each other. conflict img Conflict Resolution img of conflict</span></span>

<span key="9dab9de72e9541318e02b107556ce731"><span offset-key="9dab9de72e9541318e02b107556ce731:0">The &lt;&lt;&lt; === &gt;&gt;&gt; signs are delimiters to indicate we are separating two pieces of conflicting code. The first piece is from our Base Branch. The second piece is from our incoming branch.</span></span>

<span key="26f365dd02cf4aa4a034622af1acbb0b"><span offset-key="26f365dd02cf4aa4a034622af1acbb0b:0">--</span></span>

<span key="6e97b9c703334ccb82e55839b9514c2c"><span offset-key="6e97b9c703334ccb82e55839b9514c2c:0"><span slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span>

<span key="e24002e1dde843d8826162e047656c2e"><span offset-key="e24002e1dde843d8826162e047656c2e:0">Flashcards Node JS</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="06df349db146494abe547ac6eb6c8a5f"><span offset-key="06df349db146494abe547ac6eb6c8a5f:0">Name two objects that are available in browser runtimes but not in NodeJS.</span></span>

<span key="97aaaede8e9f44da9515baaf262645b8"><span offset-key="97aaaede8e9f44da9515baaf262645b8:0">Common answers include window, document, and location. 2. The "global object" in the Node runtime can be referenced with the name global. What name can be used in browser runtimes to reference the "global object"?</span></span>

<span key="b21e5690837444d68c42c8f84825b5b0"><span offset-key="b21e5690837444d68c42c8f84825b5b0:0">window 3. The 'fs' module contains synchronous and asynchronous versions of many of its methods. Why might one prefer to use the asynchronous versions of these methods?</span></span>

<span key="21f250fa372846ecbe1dca6faf5606d9"><span offset-key="21f250fa372846ecbe1dca6faf5606d9:0">Operations on our file system can take some time because data from our hard drive must be read or written. Performing these operations asynchronously prevents the single thread of our JavaScript program from being blocked during these operations. 4. What is the name of the node module that allows us to perform operations on our local file system?</span></span>

<span key="d9e0b688e375491497bd3e3ca4a720df"><span offset-key="d9e0b688e375491497bd3e3ca4a720df:0">fs 5. What is the name of the node module that allows us to take user input?</span></span>

<span key="6bce385164614be6bf4c7b0f238710f0"><span offset-key="6bce385164614be6bf4c7b0f238710f0:0">readline 6. What site should be used as a documentation reference for JavaScript in browser runtimes?</span></span>

<span key="1bd7429e540b4b2288d9cd6ab96f5838"><span offset-key="1bd7429e540b4b2288d9cd6ab96f5838:0">MDN, Mozilla Developer Network (</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="550227f0db3a4d05bd952254d7dd854c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="12127ed17fcc436bbce17fb30c761e4b"><span data-offset-key="12127ed17fcc436bbce17fb30c761e4b:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript</span></span></span></a><span key="01c0f5c3679644709c92110c78f4d488"><span offset-key="01c0f5c3679644709c92110c78f4d488:0">) 7. What site should be used as a documentation reference for JavaScript in the Node runtime?</span></span>

<span key="9deca345777c4223a54a3cf3da0d4dc0"><span offset-key="9deca345777c4223a54a3cf3da0d4dc0:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="http://nodejs.org" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="510dbd6eae1b4006a3150eadcef2beb3" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="421a559fa3214119a825ec370e084d9b"><span data-offset-key="421a559fa3214119a825ec370e084d9b:0">NodeJS.org</span></span></span></a><span key="0d9fd6f3b14f41b586bc51a9d122f339"><span offset-key="0d9fd6f3b14f41b586bc51a9d122f339:0"> (</span></span><a href="https://nodejs.org/api/" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="eb7692beec0c4cdda23e76b16561c9e1" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_260-2678_262-2679-240__"><span data-key="a0fd2e3d09fb45ecb6442039840ce588"><span data-offset-key="a0fd2e3d09fb45ecb6442039840ce588:0">https://nodejs.org/api/</span></span></span></a><span key="a9edcc26b0bc46c397299f5b3c3d186f"><span offset-key="a9edcc26b0bc46c397299f5b3c3d186f:0">) Git Reset</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="cf272756314c47989214f031f76c7ef2"><span offset-key="cf272756314c47989214f031f76c7ef2:0">git reset --hard</span></span>

<span key="fc48ed916c254685b2dd8f9b6be44fff"><span offset-key="fc48ed916c254685b2dd8f9b6be44fff:0">Moves HEAD ref to Discards all code changes after !</span></span>

<span key="ba8fe793c894436aa6554a9691cddd30"><span offset-key="ba8fe793c894436aa6554a9691cddd30:0">DANGEROUS! Use with caution.</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="7d3a337ab7f445e9a53df931013bb5b5"><span offset-key="7d3a337ab7f445e9a53df931013bb5b5:0">git reset --soft</span></span>

<span key="897ffbfc18944c30ac5c16e796f6eb82"><span offset-key="897ffbfc18944c30ac5c16e796f6eb82:0">Resets HEAD ref to Leaves changes in the staging area 3. git reset</span></span>

<span key="94bf9d90bce5473d9df37e3c04858781"><span offset-key="94bf9d90bce5473d9df37e3c04858781:0">Same as git reset --mixed</span></span>

<span key="6013e5df0c724959879041338860741e"><span offset-key="6013e5df0c724959879041338860741e:0">Moves HEAD ref to</span></span>

<span key="9aaf2b67b94741ed8529257d8d7a719a"><span offset-key="9aaf2b67b94741ed8529257d8d7a719a:0">Changes moved to working directory; must be re-git added.</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="fe56a69e5fd34aa387c27ca9ec7a7725"><span offset-key="fe56a69e5fd34aa387c27ca9ec7a7725:0">git reset HEAD myfile.js</span></span>

<span key="071907abd52b41f1b2330a01dff8bb0c"><span offset-key="071907abd52b41f1b2330a01dff8bb0c:0">Removes myFile.js from the staging area</span></span>

<span key="a4aa0d73f3074f56a68f646183e23b80"><span offset-key="a4aa0d73f3074f56a68f646183e23b80:0">Step 1: Attempt to replicate circumstances In software development, the first step towards debugging any issue is attempting to replicate the circumstances. With most programming languages, this is bolstered by reviewing logs leading up to an error, but with client-side JavaScript, this type of diagnosis requires significantly more foresight (more on that below).</span></span>

<span key="ad6ad4a9246b4448ad8cb918ee315b62"><span offset-key="ad6ad4a9246b4448ad8cb918ee315b62:0">Before we can replicate any circumstances of an issue, and assuming we have access to any production logs, we first need to establish some testing guidelines. This involves doing things like mimicking the production database, the user accounts involved, and even the operating system. Everything is fair game here.</span></span>

<span key="1607be1a17eb468a80e6bd32a1454949"><span offset-key="1607be1a17eb468a80e6bd32a1454949:0">Step 2: Test assumptions Once you've established the circumstances that you think might throw the exception or error you are hunting down, it's time to test them. Never test exceptions in production. Development and staging environments are designed to be breakable without any impact on the end users, so always always always try to break your code in a safe environment.</span></span>

<span key="75ff80c169084ee58019ff0d6aebfe96"><span offset-key="75ff80c169084ee58019ff0d6aebfe96:0">Step 3: Increase logging More information is always better. Using the methods described in Where are JavaScript Errors Logged?, the first step towards diagnosing any issue is to increase the amount of data you are logging. This allows you to see everything that is happening before and after a problem occurs. There is a good chance that the problems you are experiencing have potential warnings associated with them that don't necessarily make it into the logs by default.</span></span>

<span key="4e805cce6dc64678a4c3ab1e310aa64a"><span offset-key="4e805cce6dc64678a4c3ab1e310aa64a:0">Step 4: Adjust test parameters and try again If you were unable to replicate the problem in Step 2, then it's back to the drawing board. Not every error is easy to reproduce, and may have time-based constraints or something else making it difficult to replicate in a non-production environment. Jump back to Step 1, adjust your test parameters, and try it all over again.</span></span>

<span key="8af0c39610d0420899b74023fa0804fc"><span offset-key="8af0c39610d0420899b74023fa0804fc:0">What are Source Maps? In a production environment, JavaScript files are often compressed. While this is a great way to speed up any application, it can make debugging a nightmare, as the files you are trying to debug are practically unreadable. This is where source maps come into the picture. Supported by most modern browsers, a source map is a file that maps uncompressed code to compressed code, allowing you to see exactly what is going on within a production environment.</span></span>

<span key="c853e9c4ba8b4a2897473b7d01532bb2"><span offset-key="c853e9c4ba8b4a2897473b7d01532bb2:0">While most minification tools have built-in support for source maps, it is important to understand exactly how the browser connects compressed code to uncompressed code. In a nutshell, this comes in the form of a comment within a compressed JavaScript file that points directly to the source map.</span></span>

<span key="edf368e5fb49439cb1ab53dc6f1e7e0d"><span offset-key="edf368e5fb49439cb1ab53dc6f1e7e0d:0">//# sourceMappingURL=http://example.com/path/to/your/sourcemap.map As an example, let’s take a look at the developer console without source maps enabled. In particular, do you see how the source file says "Generated by CoffeeScript" and there is automatically generated JavaScript below?</span></span>

<span key="bf63d500a20a482683a77b672a81a811"><span offset-key="bf63d500a20a482683a77b672a81a811:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="61b8bc5684d4410c8e546b2387b85a3e"><span offset-key="61b8bc5684d4410c8e546b2387b85a3e:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="700fb77de7544ecd90c32006cfc760f0"><span offset-key="700fb77de7544ecd90c32006cfc760f0:0">While the production JavaScript file can be viewed and debugged it's not the code I wrote. The original source file is written in CoffeeScript, which means that any insight gleaned from the compiled code will have to be translated back into the original source file.</span></span>

<span key="85e90da2531c457798fba2293c4cd922"><span offset-key="85e90da2531c457798fba2293c4cd922:0">Now, let’s take a look at the same example with source maps enabled:</span></span>

<span key="e4f83b3f3a6c49cf838f357493905279"><span offset-key="e4f83b3f3a6c49cf838f357493905279:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="7abb365e820e4f5a8c07629427ce5e2f"><span offset-key="7abb365e820e4f5a8c07629427ce5e2f:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="b6013813564a44518cc8514dae8a0dad"><span offset-key="b6013813564a44518cc8514dae8a0dad:0">With source maps enabled, the breakpoint in the compiled script can be mapped directly to the original source file in CoffeeScript. This makes it possible to debug issues in the context of the source files, rather than the compiled and sanitized files that make it into the production environment.</span></span>

<span key="ac2a99a8ebe4478ba9d1b037da4034c1"><span offset-key="ac2a99a8ebe4478ba9d1b037da4034c1:0">Stack Traces in JavaScript Whenever exceptions are thrown, a stack trace is usually included. But, what is a stack trace? In essence, it is a rundown of every file and function that is called leading up to the error. To be clear, a stack trace doesn't include the files and functions that are touched before the error occurred, only the chain of methods that are called as the error happened. This allows you to "trace" the "stack" of operations that are performed when an error happened in order to identify exactly what went wrong, and where.</span></span>

<span key="5d9bb60c385047138baeb0c733c3c46a"><span offset-key="5d9bb60c385047138baeb0c733c3c46a:0">As an example, let's take a look at the stack trace that is returned from the following (incredibly simplistic) code:</span></span>

<span key="03eff6b4301f453e9e0190be97074c0b"><span offset-key="03eff6b4301f453e9e0190be97074c0b:0">function do\_the\_thing() { throw new Error("a thing happened!"); } do\_the\_thing(); When do\_the\_thing() is executed, an exception is immediately thrown. This results in the following stack trace:</span></span>

<span key="fb7500a78fa3474dae9fd4ffc7a2cba6"><span offset-key="fb7500a78fa3474dae9fd4ffc7a2cba6:0">Error: a thing happened! Stack trace: <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__">[email protected]</a> eval code:2:9 @debugger eval code:1:7 As you can see, rather than simply returning the exception message, reading the stack trace in reverse order shows that the exception was thrown on line 1 at column 7, but was triggered by a call to do\_the\_thing() on line 2 at column 9. For more complicated stack traces, this can be invaluable as it gives us a lot of post-mortem information.</span></span>

<span key="c53d03565e5343e292f6638ee4e865a3"><span offset-key="c53d03565e5343e292f6638ee4e865a3:0">A Brief Introduction to The Debugger While diagnosing bugs via log files works in some cases, sometimes a little more power is required. Thankfully, in most browsers it is possible to pause running scripts and step through them in order to identify issues as they happen. While doing this, it is possible to view and edit variables and properties, which gives you total control over the state of any running script in order to identify what is happening, where, and why.</span></span>

<span key="82841b7e350a4e6cadfdfb31c0a2ccc7"><span offset-key="82841b7e350a4e6cadfdfb31c0a2ccc7:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="0dc151e87ca641e6b3de7a5e43f2c218"><span offset-key="0dc151e87ca641e6b3de7a5e43f2c218:0">Developer Console Debugger</span></span>

<span key="6f7214b5982c4dbba480687d022210a5"><span offset-key="6f7214b5982c4dbba480687d022210a5:0">The browser-based debugger is an incredibly powerful tool, but the basic idea behind its use is that you add breakpoints at points in your codebase where you want to look deeper at the stack and scope of the script. When the debugger encounters these breakpoints, all execution is paused, and you are provided with the opportunity to review the values of any variables, and even modify them to better test assumptions and fix any issues you may be encountering.</span></span>

<span key="92770d7f1a944d539486b235a5885ba2"><span offset-key="92770d7f1a944d539486b235a5885ba2:0">Advanced Debugging</span></span>

<span key="e7760f988bda42c59544492bfdcd1132"><span offset-key="e7760f988bda42c59544492bfdcd1132:0">It is important to note that, while the built-in debugger is great for many use cases, the introduction of more advanced JavaScript platforms like Vue.js and Redux can make the debugger significantly more complicated to use. This is where browser-based plugins like Vue.js devtools and Redux DevTools come into play. These tools are designed with the complexities of their targeted platforms in mind, allowing for much more targeted debugging of highly complex codebases.</span></span>

<span key="cffd56a6542146dfb9b4870c47a55e98"><span offset-key="cffd56a6542146dfb9b4870c47a55e98:0">Debugging Node.js</span></span>

<span key="7884e8c3af1b40129b93455c82adce5f"><span offset-key="7884e8c3af1b40129b93455c82adce5f:0">While the browser debugger is great for client-side JavaScript, Node.js ships with its own debugger for server-side debugging. Debugging Node.js code can be accomplished by running node inspect on the source file, or through any number of great IDE integrations designed specifically for Node.js debugging.</span></span>

<span key="98a548ec13b6499dbef2d3ad775490a2"><span offset-key="98a548ec13b6499dbef2d3ad775490a2:0">Visual Studio Code Node.js Debugger</span></span>

<span key="88b554c9ffe249809384c82c331baf6b"><span offset-key="88b554c9ffe249809384c82c331baf6b:0">Visual Studio Code Node.js Debugger</span></span>

<span key="ef56fa7626b744c88993567b0b8c41fc"><span offset-key="ef56fa7626b744c88993567b0b8c41fc:0">Debugging Production Errors Using Rollbar The challenge when debugging production errors is that you do not have access to the user’s developer console. In order to gather enough context to identify the problem, you need to track information in a central location where your developers can access it. Traditionally, this is done using logs but there is a better way.</span></span>

<span key="1b691e1b0cb8427c8ec39b62ff3101bc"><span offset-key="1b691e1b0cb8427c8ec39b62ff3101bc:0">Rollbar empowers you to not only identify what is happening, but when, where, to whom, and how often. Rather than having to sort through pages of raw text logs, Rollbar aggregates data from individual exceptions and errors and creates a dashboard with as much information as possible for analyzing these issues.</span></span>

<span key="b141938a543f478784f8a4f12bf23ded"><span offset-key="b141938a543f478784f8a4f12bf23ded:0">When properly configured, these exceptions can be tied directly to user accounts, and tracked over time across an easy-to-read graph—with deployment markers to boot. While this doesn't necessarily tell you exactly what an issue is, it comes as close as possible to doing so by providing you with more information than you could possibly ask for.</span></span>

<span key="5d0239cbc33f43c5867614bb75a76fb0"><span offset-key="5d0239cbc33f43c5867614bb75a76fb0:0">Telemetry Telemetry screenshot</span></span>

<span key="ac255596016447978791c2362f12ab58"><span offset-key="ac255596016447978791c2362f12ab58:0">Unique to Rollbar's JavaScript integration, telemetry is an advanced event tracker that allows you to identify what happens in the moments leading up to, and immediately following, an error. This is incredibly valuable, as it gives you the ability to see any behavior that may have inadvertently lead to the error being thrown.</span></span>

<a href="/my-docs/v/embeds/aesthetic/untitled" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1awozwy r-14lw9ot r-190qawg r-z2wwpe r-rs99b7 r-4dj0k7 r-1loqt21 r-1quu1zo r-1ro0kt6 r-18u37iz r-16y2uox r-1wbh5a2 r-nsbfu8 r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"></a>

Test Dirven Development:

<a href="/my-docs/v/embeds/#overview" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-855088 r-dwliz8 r-1loqt21 r-18u37iz r-lqms97 r-dnmrzs r-iphfwy r-1guathk r-1h8ys4a r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr r-7xmw5f"></a>

Overview
